Divine Transcendence
beginner
6 min
Proofs for Divine Transcendence
Sanusi proves God is not a body, not an accident, not united, and not in a direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proofs that God is not a body, not an accident, not united with anything, and not in any direction.

Core Idea
God's transcendence is proven by the impossibility of His being like anything contingent.

Sanusi now moves from general attributes to specific negations. He provides concise rational arguments that the Creator cannot be a body, an accident, united with another, or located in a direction. Each proof relies on the simple logical principle that whatever is contingent cannot be the Necessary Being. This passage is a classic example of the kalam method.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Examine the first proof: not a body or accident
Identify why the Maker cannot be a body (jism) or an accident (sifa) of a body. The reason given is that bodies and their accidents are all originated (mustahdath), and the Creator is not originated.
This proof relies on the previously established principle of origination (huduth).
3
Examine the second proof: not united with another
Understand the logical argument against union (ittihad). The text explores two possibilities: if both entities remain, they are two; if one or both cease, union is impossible because the non-existent cannot unite with the existent.
This is a disjunctive syllogism covering all possibilities.
4
Examine the third proof: not in any direction
Understand why God cannot be in a direction (jiha). The proof is that directions are only inhabited by bodies, and God is not a body. Moreover, directions themselves are accidents of bodily organs.
This argument also implies that God does not have a direction Himself.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how these three proofs collectively establish God's absolute dissimilarity to contingent things (mukhalafa lil hawadith). Each proof negates a category of contingency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب
الدلیل علی وجوب مخالفته تعالى للحوادث
و عدم اتحاده بغيره ، وبيان الدليل على وجوب قيامه تعالى بنفسه
ويلزم أيضاً : أنْ يكونَ محدث العالم ليس بجسم ولا صفة للجسم ؛ لما عرفت من وجوب الحدوث للأجرام وصفاتها
ولا متحداً بغيره ؛ أي : يكون معه واحداً ، وإلا فإن بقيا موجودين فهما بعد اثنان لا واحد ، وإن لم يبقيا موجودين لم يتحدا أيضاً ؛ لأنه إن عدم كل منهما ووجد ثالث فظاهر ، وإن عدم أحدهما وبقي الآخر فكذلك ؛ لأن المعدوم لا يتحد بالموجود .
وأن يكون ليس في جهة من الجهات ؛ لأنه لا يعمرها إلا الأجرام ، وألا تكون له هو أيضاً جهة ؛ لأنها من عوارض الجسم ؛ فوق من عوارض عضو الرأس ، وتحت من عوارض عضو الرجل ، ويمين من عوارض العضو الأيمن ، وشمال من عوارض العضو الأيسر ، وأمام من عوارض
Chapter: The proof for the obligation of His dissimilarity to contingent things (mukhalafa lil hawadith) and His non-unity with another, and an explanation of the proof for the obligation of His self-subsistence (qiyamuhu binafsihi). And it also follows that the maker of the world is not a body (jism) nor an accident (sifa) of a body; because you already know the obligation of origination (huduth) for bodies and their accidents. And He is not united (mutahid) with another, i.e., that He would be one with it; for if both remain existing, then they are two, not one; and if they do not both remain existing, they also have not united; because if both are annihilated and a third exists, it is obvious; and if one is annihilated and the other remains, similarly, because the non-existent cannot unite with the existent. And He is not in any direction (jiha), because nothing inhabits directions except bodies; and He also does not have a direction, because directions are accidents of the body: above is an accident of the head, below is an accident of the foot, right is an accident of the right limb, left is an accident of the left limb, and front is an accident of ...
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents proofs for God's transcendence above created attributes. It begins with the heading stating the topic: proof for God's dissimilarity to created things, His non-unity with another, and His self-subsistence (qiyamuhu binafsihi). The first proof: the Maker is neither a body (jism) nor an accident (sifa) of a body. The reason given is that bodies and their accidents are all originated (mustahdath), as established earlier. Since the Creator is not originated, He cannot be a body or an accident. The second proof: He is not united (mutahid) with another. The argument examines two possibilities for union: either both entities remain or they do not. If both remain, they are still two, not one. If they do not both remain, i.e., one or both cease to exist, then union does not occur either. If both are annihilated and a third thing comes into being, that is not union. If one is annihilated and the other remains, the non-existent cannot unite with the existent. Therefore, union is impossible. The third proof: He is not in any direction (jiha). The reason is that directions are only inhabited by bodies, and He is not a body. Moreover, directions themselves are accidents of the body: 'above' relates to the head, 'below' to the foot, 'right' to the right side, 'left' to the left side, and 'front' (the text is cut off here) are all accidents of bodily organs. Hence, a non-bodily being cannot be in a direction. Each proof reinforces that the Creator is fundamentally unlike His creation.

Key Terms
مخالفة للحوادث (mukhalafat lil hawadith)
جسم (jism)
صفة (sifa)
اتحاد (ittihad)
جهة (jiha)
عوارض الجسم (awarid al-jism)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'not in a direction' means God is nowhere or does not exist.
Correction: The proof shows that direction is an accident of bodies; God, being non-bodily, transcends spatial categories. He is not 'nowhere' in a spatial sense, but rather beyond spatial reference entirely.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi argue that the Creator cannot be united (mutahid) with another thing?
A) Because union would require both to be bodies.
B) Because if both remain they are two, and if one ceases they cannot unite.
C) Because union is only possible between opposites.
D) Because the Creator is self-sufficient and cannot combine.

Key Takeaway
God is absolutely unlike His creation: He is not a body, not an accident, not united with anything, and not in any direction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that God is not in any direction. When you pray, do you ever catch yourself thinking of God as 'up there'? How can you retrain your heart to feel His presence without resorting to a spatial image?
?
The proof against union with another shows that God cannot blend with anything. Where in your life do you subtly 'unite' something—like status, wealth, or relationships—with your sense of worth or security? How would uprooting that change your reliance on God alone?
?
If God is not a body and has no parts, what does that mean for how you imagine His anger, love, or mercy? Can you worship a God who has no 'right hand' or 'throne' in the physical sense, yet is fully real? Commit to memorizing one of these proofs to say when you feel your heart slipping into anthropomorphism.

Divine Transcendence
beginner
4 min
Proof that the Creator is not a Body or an Accident
Sanusi introduces the chapter and proves the creator is not a body or accident.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational proof for God's transcendence over bodies and accidents, based on their contingency.

Core Idea
Everything contingent cannot be the creator; bodies and accidents are contingent.

This chapter opens a critical section on divine transcendence. Sanusi begins by stating three necessary attributes for the Creator, then offers a concise logical argument that the Creator cannot be a body or an accident. The reasoning rests on a principle already established: all bodies and accidents are contingent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the chapter heading lists three topics.
2
Identify the three topics in the heading
The heading mentions: God's opposition to contingent things, His non-unification with another, and His self-subsistence. These are attributes of transcendence.
3
Understand the logical entailment
The passage then states that it follows (يلزم) that the originator of the world is not a body or an accident. Ask yourself: why does this follow?
The reason is given next.
4
Connect contingency to the conclusion
The reason given is that you already know bodies and accidents are contingent. Since contingent things depend on a creator, the creator cannot be contingent itself.
This is a basic kalam argument: the creator must be unlike created things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب
الدلیل علی وجوب مخالفته تعالى للحوادث
و عدم اتحاده بستره [؟]، وبيان الدليل على وجوب قیامه تعالی بنفسه
ويلزم أيضاً: أنْ يكونَ مُحدث العالم ليسَ بجِرْمٍ ولا صفة للجرم؛ لما عرفتَ مِنْ وجوب الحدوث للأجرام
وصفاتها
Chapter: The proof of the obligation of the Most High's opposition to contingent things and His non-unification with His covering [بستره?], and the exposition of the proof of the obligation of His being self-subsistent. And it also follows: that the originator of the world is not a body nor an accident of a body, because you have known the necessity of contingency for bodies and their accidents.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage combines a chapter heading and the first proof. The heading announces three topics: God's opposition to contingent things (i.e., His transcendence), His not being united with another, and His being self-subsistent. The first proof is that the creator (مُحدث العالم) is neither a body (جرم) nor an accident (صفة) of a body. The reason is that you have already learned that bodies and their accidents are all contingent (حادث). Since every contingent requires a creator, and the creator cannot itself be contingent, He cannot be a body or accident. This is a foundational argument for divine transcendence.

Key Terms
مُحدث العالم
جرم
صفة
الحدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think God is a body.
Correction: This proof shows that bodies are contingent and thus cannot be the creator, so God cannot be a body.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for proving that the creator is not a body or an accident?
A) Because bodies are eternal.
B) Because bodies and accidents are contingent.
C) Because God is self-subsistent.
D) Because union is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The creator must be unlike bodies and accidents because they are contingent, while He is necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God were a body, He would be limited in space and time. How does the certainty that He is not a body affect the way you perceive His power over creation? In what specific moments this week have you unconsciously pictured God as something material? What will you do to purify your conception of Him?
?
This proof depends entirely on the premise that bodies and accidents are contingent. Do you accept this truth in your mind, but does your heart still feel doubts? When you see the vast universe, do you truly believe it had a beginning, or does a lingering assumption of eternity creep in? How can you strengthen your conviction?
?
Since the Creator is not like anything He has made, what does that demand of you in worship? Are there any acts where you treat God as if He needs something from you, or as if He is located in a specific direction? Commit to one practical step this week that acknowledges His absolute transcendence in your daily life.

Divine Transcendence

Proof that God is Not United with Another
Sanusi presents a logical dilemma refuting divine union.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof against the possibility of God being united with another being.

Core Idea
Union with God is logically impossible in every scenario.

Sanusi now tackles a subtle theological mistake: the idea that God could become 'one' with another being through union. He presents a succinct logical dilemma showing that no matter how union is imagined, it fails. This reinforces Allah's absolute oneness and transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise, logical style typical of Sanusi.
2
Trace the two main scenarios
Identify the two exhaustive possibilities: both existent after union, or not both existent. For each, see why union fails.
The argument is a classic dilemma (disjunction).
3
Connect to divine oneness
Ask yourself: why is this argument important for tawhid? How does it protect Allah's uniqueness?
This connects to the broader theme of divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا مُتَّحِداً بغيرِهِ؛ أي: يكون معه واحداً، وإلا فإنْ بقيا موجودين فهما بعد اثنان لا واحد، وإن لم يبقيا موجودين لم يتحدا أيضاً؛ لأَنَّهُ إِنْ عُدِمَ كلٌّ منهما ووُجِدَ ثالث فظاهرُ، وإنْ عُدِمَ أحدهما وبقي الآخر فكذلكَ؛ لأنَّ المعدوم لا يتَّحد بالموجود.
And He is not united with another; meaning: that He be one with it. Otherwise, if both remain existent, then they are two, not one; and if they do not remain existent, they also do not unite, because if each of them is annihilated and a third is found, it is obvious; and if one of them is annihilated and the other remains, it is likewise, because the non-existent does not unite with the existent.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This is a proof by disjunction (dilemma) against the possibility of God uniting with another being. The author presents two exhaustive scenarios: (1) If both God and the other remain existent after union, then there are two entities, not one, so no real union occurs. (2) If they do not both remain, then either both are annihilated and a third comes into existence (clearly not union), or one is annihilated and the other remains—but non-existence cannot unite with existence. Therefore, union is impossible in all cases.

Key Terms
اتحاد
متحّد
معدوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Two beings can become one by blending or merging.
Correction: The proof shows that no matter how you conceive it, union leads to a logical contradiction or impossibility.

Checkpoint
If God were united with another being and both cease to exist, what happens?
A) They become one.
B) They become two.
C) A third being appears.
D) No union occurs because non-existence cannot unite with existence.

Key Takeaway
The only way two things become one is impossible; thus God cannot unite with any other.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allāh is One', do you truly believe that nothing can be added to or subtracted from His essence? Does your heart affirm that He is absolutely unique, or do you sometimes imagine Him in human terms that imply composition? Commit to reciting 'Qul Huwa Allāhu Aḥad' with full awareness of this proof.
?
Have you ever, even subconsciously, attributed any partner to Allah in your intentions or desires—like seeking approval of people more than His pleasure? How does the logical impossibility of union challenge you to purify your tawhid in daily life? Resolve to check your intentions before every action today.
?
If non-existence cannot unite with existence, then nothing can become 'part of God'. How does this truth affect the way you seek closeness to Him—not through fusion, but through obedience and love? Will you shift from hoping for mystical union to seeking His good pleasure through following His commands?

Divine Transcendence

Proof that God is Not in Any Direction
Sanusi proves God cannot be in a spatial direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God cannot be located in a spatial direction, based on the reasoning that directions are accidents of bodily organs and only bodies occupy directions.

Core Idea
Direction is a property of bodies; the non-bodily Creator has no direction.

Sanusi presents a concise argument for God's transcendence of space. He shows that direction (جهة) is tied to specific bodily organs, and since God is not a body, He cannot be in a direction. This argument safeguards tawhid from anthropomorphic conceptions of God.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing, then read the literal translation. Let the logical flow sink in before analyzing.
Notice how Sanusi uses a list of directions to show their link to body parts.
2
Analyze the argument structure
Identify the two premises: (1) only bodies occupy directions, and (2) directions are accidents of bodily organs. Then see how the conclusion follows: a non-body cannot have direction.
The six directions are each tied to a specific organ.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider why this matters for Islamic theology: it refutes any literal spatial attribute for God, preserving His absolute transcendence.
This argument is part of a larger proof that God is not a body.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنْ يكونَ ليس في جهةٍ مِنَ الجهاتِ؛ لأَنَّهُ لا يعمرُها إلا الأجرام، وألا تكونَ له هو أيضاً جهة؛ لأنَّها مِنْ عوارض الجسم؛ ففوقٌ مِنْ عوارض عضو الرأس، وتحت مِنْ عوارض عضْوِ الرِّجْلِ، ويمينُ مِنْ عوارض العضو الأيمن، وشمالٌ مِنْ عوارض العضوِ الأيسر، وأمامٌ مِنْ عوارض البطْنِ، وخلفٌ مِنْ عوارضِ الظَّهِرِ، ومَنِ استحالَ عليهِ أَنْ يكونَ جِرْماً.. استحالَ أنْ يتّصف بهذه الأعضاء ولوازمها على الضرورة.
And that He is not in any direction of the directions, because only bodies occupy them. And that He also does not have a direction, because directions are accidents of the body. For 'above' is an accident of the head organ, 'below' is an accident of the foot organ, 'right' is an accident of the right organ, 'left' is an accident of the left organ, 'front' is an accident of the belly, and 'back' is an accident of the back. And whoever it is impossible to be a body, it is impossible for him to be described with these organs and their necessary concomitants, necessarily.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage gives two reasons why God cannot be in a direction. First, only bodies occupy directions (جهات) like above, below, etc. Second, direction itself is an accident (عرض) of bodily organs—'above' is an accident of the head, 'below' of the foot, etc. Since God is not a body, He cannot have these organs, and therefore cannot have the accidents that belong to them. The conclusion is necessary: a non-body cannot have direction.

Key Terms
جهة
عوارض الجسم
جرم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe God is literally 'above' in a spatial sense, e.g., above the heavens.
Correction: This passage shows that 'above' is an accident of the head, so it cannot apply to God, who is not a body.

Checkpoint
Why can God not be in a direction?
A) Because directions are accidents of bodily organs.
B) Because He is self-subsistent.
C) Because He is eternal.
D) Because He has no beginning.

Key Takeaway
God is not in any direction because direction is an attribute of bodies, and God is not a body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You intellectually know God has no direction, but in your heart, do you ever catch yourself picturing Him 'up there' when you pray? How can you actively train your mind to rid itself of such imagery based on this proof?
?
If direction is a property of physical bodies, and God has no direction, then He is utterly unlike anything you perceive. Does your worship reflect this absolute uniqueness, or do you sometimes treat God as if He were a larger, more powerful version of a created being? What specific habit can you change today to deepen your tanzih (transcendence)?
?
The proof says it is 'necessarily' (على الضرورة) impossible for a non-body to have direction. Do you feel the weight of that necessity in your soul? If you truly believed that, would you ever fall into thinking God is literally 'above' or 'in' a place? What would it take for you to internalize this so deeply that it transforms your dua? Write down one concrete action you will take this week to remind yourself of this truth.

Divine Transcendence
intermediate

God's Actions Have No Purpose or Cause
Sanusi argues that divine actions and rulings have no ulterior purpose or cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi insists that God's actions and rulings have no purpose or cause, and why this is a core principle of Ash'ari theology.

Core Idea
God's actions are purely by choice, not for any external purpose or cause.

Sanusi now tackles a key Ash'ari doctrine: divine acts are not motivated by any purpose or cause. This might seem strange—after all, we often ask 'why' about God's actions. But Sanusi argues that attributing purpose to God implies deficiency or obligation, which is impossible. In this passage, he lays out the reasoning clearly, showing that divine commands and rulings are known only through revelation, not reason. Let's unpack this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the flow: Sanusi starts with a general statement, then gives two parallel arguments: one about creation, one about rulings.
Pay attention to the phrase 'بمحض الاختيار' (by pure choice).
2
Identify the two main arguments
Sanusi argues (1) that there is no purpose (gharad) in creation, and (2) that there is no purpose for His rulings (ahkam). For each, he explains why purpose would be impossible.
The phrase 'وكما استحال... كذلك استحال' links the two.
3
Understand the equality of all actions
The key premise is that all actions are equal in being God's creation. Therefore, any differentiation (e.g., this act is obligatory, that is prohibited) cannot be due to any inherent quality—it is pure choice.
This refutes the idea that reason can determine moral value.
4
Grasp the conclusion and its implications
Sanusi concludes that divine acts have no 'illa (cause). Any causal language in scripture must be interpreted metaphorically as 'indications' (amarat). This affirms God's absolute transcendence and free will.
This is a cornerstone of Ash'ari theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في ذاتِهِ مُتكملاً بفعلِهِ ، وذلكَ محال ، ولا لغرض لخلْقِهِ وإلا وجب عليهِ مراعاة الصلاح والأصلح لهم ، وهو محال لما سيأتي . وكما استحالَ أنْ يريد سبحانه أو يفعل لغرض .. . كذلك استحالَ أنْ يكونَ حكمه على فعل بوجوب أو تحريم أو غيرهما مِنَ الأحكام الشرعيَّةِ لغرضِ مِنَ الأعْراضِ ؛ لأنَّ الأفعال كلَّها مستويةٌ في أنَّها خلقه واختراعُهُ ، فتعينُ بعضها للإيجاب وبعضها للتحريم أو غيره.. واقع بمحض الاختيار ، لا سبب له ولا مجال للعقل فيه أصلاً ، وإِنَّما يُعرَفُ بالشرع فقط . وبالجملة : فأفعالُهُ تعالى وأحكامه لا علة لها وما يُوجَدُ مِنَ التعليلِ لذلكَ في كلام أهل الشرعِ فَمُؤوَّلٌ بالأمارات أو نحوها مما يصح
That He is perfect in His essence by His action is impossible. And there is no purpose for His creating; otherwise, He would be obliged to observe what is best and most suitable for them, which is impossible for what will come. And just as it is impossible that He, exalted, should will or act for a purpose, likewise it is impossible that His judgment on an act—whether of obligation, prohibition, or other legal rulings—be for a purpose among purposes. For all actions are equal in being His creation and invention. Therefore, the specification of some for obligation and others for prohibition or other [rulings] occurs by pure choice, having no cause, and the intellect has no scope in it at all; rather, it is known only by revelation. In summary: His exalted acts and rulings have no cause, and what is found of attribution of cause for that in the speech of the people of revelation is interpreted allegorically as indications or the like that is valid.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is an argument that God's actions and rulings have no purpose or cause. The author begins by stating that it is impossible for God to be perfect in His essence by His action—meaning His essence does not need His actions to become perfect. Then he asserts that there is no purpose (gharad) for His creating; if there were, He would be bound to choose what is most beneficial for creation, which is impossible. The same impossibility applies to His rulings: they are not motivated by any external purpose, because all actions are equally His creation. The differentiation of some acts as obligatory and others as prohibited is purely by His choice, without any cause, and reason has no access to it—only revelation informs us. The author concludes that divine acts and rulings have no 'illa (cause), and any apparent causal explanation in religious texts must be interpreted allegorically (ta'wil) as signs, not real causes.

Key Terms
غرض
علة
اختيار
محض
تعليل
أمارات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's actions have rational causes or that He is obliged to do what is best for creation.
Correction: The passage shows that all actions are equal as His creation; differentiation is by pure choice, not any cause or obligation.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is it impossible for God's actions and rulings to have a purpose?
A) Because purposes imply deficiency in His essence.
B) Because all actions are equal in being His creation, so no external reason can differentiate them.
C) Because revelation contradicts the idea of purpose.
D) Both A and B.

Key Takeaway
God's actions and rulings have no cause or purpose; they are purely by His choice, known only through revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a divine command that seems irrational to you, do you resent God for not providing a reason? Will you submit purely because He chose it, or do you demand a purpose?
?
Is there a trial in your life where you have secretly believed God owes you an explanation? How does the truth that His actions have no cause challenge your heart to trust without understanding?
?
Are you comfortable with a faith that places revelation above your own reasoning, even when the basis of a ruling is hidden? Can you worship a God whose decrees are purely by His choice, with no justification accessible to your intellect?

Proof That God Cannot Possess Temporal Attributes
Sanusi proves God cannot have temporal attributes and refutes an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that God cannot be described with temporal attributes and why the objection of successive attributes fails.

Core Idea
A temporal attribute would make God temporal—contradicting His necessary eternity.

Sanusi presents a rigorous argument to defend God's transcendence. He demonstrates that if God were to acquire a new attribute over time, it would necessitate His own temporality or imperfection. He then refutes a subtle objection involving infinite regress. This lesson unpacks that reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let Sanusi's own argument unfold naturally.
Notice the two distinct proofs and the objection-refutation structure.
2
Identify the two proofs
Sanusi gives two arguments: (1) If God had a temporal attribute, He would be temporal because what is not free from temporal events is temporal. (2) That temporal attribute would be a perfection missing from God in pre-eternity, implying imperfection.
The first proof uses the principle that the eternal does not cease.
3
Examine the objection and refutation
The objector says God might acquire perfections successively without beginning. Sanusi refutes this by noting it leads to an infinite regress of temporal events with no beginning, which is impossible.
This objection is about 'tasalsul' – an infinite chain of temporal events.
4
Understand the final point
Sanusi concludes that each attribute must be one; otherwise, there would be two identical attributes (like two eternals) – which is impossible (tahsil al-hasil).
This reinforces the impossibility of multiple temporal attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو مثلها لا يكون إلا حادثاً ؛ بدليل طريانِ عدمِهِ ؛ إذ القديم لا ينعدم ، وما لا يعرى عن الحوادثِ يكون حادثاً ضرورةً ، فلزمَ أنَّهُ لو اتّصف تعالى بصفة حادثة لوجبَ حدوثه ضرورةً ، وقد عرفت وجوبَ قدمِهِ جلَّ وعلا . وأيضاً : فهو جلَّ وعزَّ لا يتّصفُ إلا بالكمال إجماعاً ، فيلزمُ في هذه الصفة الحادثة التي فُرِضَ اتِّصافُهُ تعالى بها أن تكونَ مِنْ صفاتِ الكمال ، وقد فاتَتْ ذاتَهُ العليَّةَ في الأزلِ ؛ لفَرْضِ حدوثِها ، وفوتُ الكمال نقص ، وهو تعالى مُنزَّه عنه بإجماع العقلاء ولا يُعترَضُ على هذا : بأَنَّهُ لا يلزم منه فوتُ الذاتِ العليَّةِ كمالُ هذه الصفة الحادثة ؛ لاحتمال اتصافه بأمثالها على التوالي لا إلى أوَّلِ ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : لا يخفى أنَّ هذا الاحتمال باطل ؛ لأنَّهُ تسلسل مِنْ بابِ حوادث لا أَوَّلَ لها وهو ظاهر الاستحالة ويلزمُ أنْ تكونَ كلَّ صفةٍ مِنْ صفاتِهِ تعالى واحدةً ، وإلا لزم اجتماعُ المثلين ، وتحصيل الحاصل ، وهو محال .
Or like it cannot be but temporal; by the evidence of the occurrence of its non-existence; for the eternal does not cease to exist, and that which is not free from temporal occurrences is necessarily temporal. So it follows that if the Exalted were described with a temporal attribute, His temporality would be necessitated necessarily, and you have known the necessity of His pre-eternity, may He be glorified and exalted. Also: He, glorified and exalted, is described only with perfection by consensus, so it follows that this temporal attribute with which the Exalted is supposed to be described must be among the attributes of perfection, and it was absent from His sublime essence in pre-eternity due to the supposition of its temporality, and absence of perfection is deficiency, and the Exalted is free from it by consensus of the rational people. And this is not objected to by saying: that the absence of the sublime essence from the perfection of this temporal attribute does not necessarily follow; due to the possibility of His being described with its likes successively without beginning; because we say: it is not hidden that this possibility is false because it is an infinite regress (tasalsul) from the category of occurrences with no beginning, and it is clearly impossible. And it follows that every attribute of His, the Exalted, must be one, otherwise there would follow the conjunction of two similars and the attainment of the attained (tahsil al-hasil), which is impossible.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a proof against God being described with temporal attributes. The author argues that if God had a temporal attribute, He would be temporal because the eternal does not cease to exist, and anything associated with temporal things is temporal. He also argues by perfection: God is described only with perfection by consensus, so the supposed temporal attribute would have to be a perfection that was absent from God in pre-eternity, implying deficiency, which is impossible for God. An objection is raised: perhaps God acquires such perfections successively with no beginning. The author refutes this by noting that it leads to an infinite regress of temporal events that has no beginning, which is impossible. Finally, he states that each attribute must be singular; otherwise, there would be two identical attributes simultaneously, which is impossible. This refutes any attempt to argue for multiple temporal attributes.

Key Terms
حادث
قديم
تسلسل
مثلين
تحصيل الحاصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God could acquire new perfections over time without beginning, thus avoiding the problem of deficiency.
Correction: This is false because it leads to an infinite regress of temporal events with no beginning, which is impossible. Moreover, it would require multiple identical attributes, which is also impossible.

Checkpoint
What is the main proof that God cannot have a temporal attribute?
A) Because the eternal does not cease to exist, and what is not free from temporal events is temporal.
B) Because temporal attributes are imperfections.
C) Because God's attributes are all eternal.
D) The objection shows it is possible.

Key Takeaway
God cannot have temporal attributes because it would entail His own temporality or imperfection; the objection of successive attributes fails due to the impossibility of infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make du'a, do you ever ask Allah to become more merciful or more powerful? How does this lesson reveal that your request misunderstands His eternal perfection? What should your du'a become instead?
?
If you truly believe that God cannot acquire new attributes, then what does it mean when you feel your knowledge of Him grows? Is He really 'showing you more of Himself'? How can you embrace the truth that He has always been fully perfect without any hidden part waiting to be revealed?
?
The argument uses the impossibility of infinite regress to stop any attempt to add to God. When you think about your own sins and need for forgiveness, do you expect God to 'become' more forgiving as you repent? How does this lesson call you to a deeper reliance on His eternally perfect mercy—already complete before you ever existed?

Proof of God's Oneness in Essence
Sanusi proves God's oneness in essence by refuting composition and indivisible atom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God must be one in essence, meaning not composed of parts, and why this does not mean He is an indivisible atom.

Core Idea
God's oneness means no parts, not an indivisible speck.

Sanusi begins a chapter proving God's oneness. He establishes that all things depend directly on God. Then he focuses on the essential oneness: God is not composed of parts. He provides a logical argument against composition and clarifies that this does not reduce God to an indivisible atom.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the overall claim: God is one in essence.
Pay attention to the final clarification about indivisible atoms.
2
Identify the composition argument
Find the two possibilities if God were composed of parts and their consequences. Understand why both are impossible.
The argument uses a dichotomy: either every part has divine attributes (multiple gods) or only some (need a specifier → contingent).
3
Distinguish from indivisible atom
Notice that Sanusi explicitly denies that negating composition means affirming an indivisible atom, which is still a body.
Indivisible atoms are still subject to magnitude, which is impossible for God.
4
Connect to divine transcendence
Reflect on how this argument shows that God is beyond physical categories like size or composition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الدليل على وجوب الوحدانية له جل وعلا و وجوب استناد الكائنات كلها إليه ابتداء بلا واسطة آلة له منها ولامعين وأنه ليس في الوجود إلا الله سبحانه وأفعاله ويلزمُ أنْ يكونَ تعالى واحداً في ذاتِهِ ؛ بمعنى : أَنَّهُ غيرُ مُركَّب ، وإلا لزم أن يكون جسماً ، وأيضاً : فلو تركَّبَ مِنْ : جزأين فأكثر لم يخلُ : إِمَّا أنْ يقوم بكل جزء صفاتُ الألوهية ، أو يختص قيامها بالبعض ، والأوَّلُ يلزم منه تعدد الآلهة ، والثاني يلزم منه الحدوث ؛ للاحتياج إلى المخصِّص بعضها بصفاتِ الألوهية ؛ لاستواء جميعها في قبول تلك الصفاتِ وليس معنى نفي التركيب في الذاتِ العليَّةِ أنَّها جزء لا يتجزأ ، وإلا لزمَ أنْ تكون جوهراً فرداً ، وقد سبق استحالةُ الجرْمِيَّةِ عليهِ مطلقاً ، وإِنَّما المقصودُ : أَنَّ الذات العليَّةَ لا تقبلُ صِغَراً ولا كِبَراً ؛ لأنَّهما مِنْ عوارض الأجرام ، وهو تعالى يستحيلُ أنْ يكونَ جِرْماً
Chapter: The proof of the necessity of oneness for Him, Exalted and Glorified, and the necessity of the dependence of all things upon Him initially without any instrument from them and without intermediaries, and that there is nothing in existence except Allah, Sublime, and His actions. And it necessarily follows that He, Exalted, is one in His essence; meaning: that He is not composed, otherwise it would necessitate that He be a body. Also: if He were composed of two or more parts, it would not be free from: either the attributes of divinity subsist in every part, or their subsistence is specific to some parts. The first entails the multiplicity of gods, and the second entails temporal origination (huduth); due to the need for a specifier for some of them to possess the attributes of divinity, since all parts are equal in their capacity for those attributes. And the meaning of negating composition (tarkib) in the Supreme Essence is not that It is an indivisible part, otherwise it would necessitate that It be an indivisible atom (jawhar fard), and the impossibility of corporeality (jismiyya) for Him absolutely has preceded. Rather, the intended meaning is that the Supreme Essence does not accept smallness or largeness; because they are accidents of bodies, and He, Exalted, cannot possibly be a body (jirm).
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the overarching thesis of the chapter: the proof that God alone is necessarily one, that all things depend on Him directly with no intermediate, and that nothing truly exists except God and His actions. It then focuses on the first implication—God's oneness in essence. The author explains that this oneness means God is not compound (murakkab); if He were composite, He would have to be a body. He then provides a logical proof: if God were composed of parts, either every part would possess the attributes of divinity or only some would. If every part had these attributes, there would be multiple gods. If only some parts had them, then those parts would need a specifier to be distinguished from the others, implying contingency (huduth) and thus temporality. The passage then clarifies that negating composition does not mean affirming an indivisible atom (jawhar fard), as that would still imply a body. Rather, the negation of composition means the Divine Essence has no magnitude—neither small nor large—since those are accidents of bodies, and God cannot be a body.

Key Terms
وحدانية
تركيب
جوهر فرد
جرم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Negating composition means God is an indivisible atom.
Correction: An indivisible atom is still a body with magnitude; God is beyond all magnitude.

Checkpoint
In the argument against composition, what are the two possibilities if God were composed of parts?
A) Either God is a body or He is not.
B) Either each part has divine attributes (leading to multiple gods) or only some parts have them (leading to contingency).
C) Either God is a simple indivisible atom or He is composite.
D) Either God has no attributes or He has all attributes.

Key Takeaway
God's oneness in essence means He is not composed of parts, and this does not imply He is an indivisible atom, as that would still be a body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You say you worship the One God, but do you ever mentally divide His attributes—acting as if His mercy is separate from His justice? This lesson proves He is not composed of parts. What would it mean for you to worship Him as undivided?
?
The passage argues that if God were composed of parts, He would need a specifier and thus be temporal. In your own life, do you treat God as if He can be 'managed' by focusing on one aspect of His nature while ignoring others? How does this lesson challenge you to submit to His absolute oneness?
?
Rejecting the indivisible atom still leaves you with a God who has no magnitude at all—neither small nor large. Can you honestly say you relate to a God who is beyond all measurement? If not, what concrete step will you take today to remind yourself that He is not a body?

Divine Transcendence

The Proof of God's Oneness in Attributes
Sanusi proves God's oneness in attributes and refutes polytheism with two rational arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's arguments for why God must be one in His attributes and why polytheism is rationally impossible.

Core Idea
If there were two gods, neither could act.

Sanusi presents a two-step proof: first, that having a 'like' would imply contingency; second, that a second divine being would inevitably lead to incapacity. This lesson unpacks the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, then its translation. Notice the logical connectors like 'وايضا' and 'فإن'.
The argument uses conditional reasoning: 'if... then...'.
2
Identify the two arguments
Find the argument against having a 'like' (مثل) and the separate argument against a second god. Note the key difference: the first is about attributes, the second about divine status.
3
Understand the consequences
Consider why a second god would lead to incapacity in both scenarios (disagreement and agreement). How does this prove God's oneness?
The conclusion that nothing would exist is an absurdity that refutes the premise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويلزمُ أيضاً : أنْ يكونَ تعالى واحداً في صفاته ؛ بمعنى : أنَّهُ لا مثلَ لهُ ، وإلا لزم الحدوث ؛ لاحتياج كل مِنَ المِثْلَينِ إِلى مَنْ يُخصِّصُهُ بالعارض الذي يمتاز به عن مثله وأيضاً : لو كانَ معَهُ ثانٍ في الأُلُوهِيَّةِ للزمَ أَنْ يكونَ ذلكَ الثاني عام القدرةِ والإرادَةِ مثلَهُ ، وذلكَ يؤدّي إلى اتِّصافِ أحدهما بالعجز ضرورةً ، سواء اختلفا على التضاد ـ وهو ظاهر - أوِ اتَّفقا ؛ لأنَّ الفعل الواحد يستحيل انقسامه ، فلا يمكن أن يقع إلا مِنْ أحدهما ؛ فيلزم عجز الآخر الذي لم يقع منه ، وإذا عجز أحدهما وجب عجز الآخر لتماثلهما ، وذلك يؤدّي إلى ألا يُوجَدَ شيءٌ مِنَ العالم ، والعيانُ يُكذِّبُهُ وبهذا الدليل تعرفُ استحالة أن يكون لشيءٍ مِنَ العالم تأثير البتةَ في أثر ما ؛ لما يلزمُ عليهِ مِنْ خروج ذلك الأثر عن قدرةِ مولانا جلَّ وعزَّ وإرادتِهِ ، وذلكَ يُوجِبُ أنْ يغلبَ الحادث القديم ، وهو محال فلا أثرَ إذاً لقدرةِ المخلوقِ في حركة ولا سكون ، ولا طاعة ولا معصية، ولا في أثر ما على العموم ، لا مباشرةً ولا تولداً
And it also necessarily follows that He, Exalted, is one in His attributes; meaning: that He has no like (mithl), otherwise temporality (huduth) would follow; because each of the two likes would need someone to specify it with the accident by which it is distinguished from its like. Also: if there were a second in divinity with Him, it would necessitate that that second be equal to Him in power and will, and that leads necessarily to one of them being characterized by incapacity ('ajz) — whether they disagree (in which case it is obvious) or they agree; because a single action cannot be divided, so it can only occur from one of them; thus incapacity of the other from whom it did not occur follows, and if one is incapable, the other must be incapable due to their similarity, and that leads to nothing of the world existing, but ocular evidence contradicts this. And by this proof you know the impossibility of anything in the world having any effect whatsoever in any trace; because that would necessitate that trace's departure from the power and will of our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, and that would require the temporal to prevail over the eternal, which is impossible. So there is no effect, therefore, for the power of the created being in any movement or stillness, nor in any obedience or disobedience, nor in any effect at all in general, whether directly or indirectly (tawallud).
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument proving God's oneness in attributes and then drawing a critical conclusion about causality. The author first states that God must be one in His attributes, meaning He has no equal or like. The proof: if there were two likes, each would need a specific cause to distinguish it from the other, which would imply contingency and thus temporality. Then the author provides a sharper proof against polytheism: if there were a second god, it would have to share God's complete power and will. In any scenario—whether the two gods disagree or agree—one of them must be incapable. If they disagree over a contradictory action, only one can act, so the other is incapable. If they agree on a single action, the action cannot be performed by both, so again only one acts. Therefore, one is incapable, and since they are alike, both must be incapable. This leads to the conclusion that nothing in the world would exist, but the observable existence of the world refutes that. The author then says: 'By this proof you know that no created thing has any effect at all.' This is because if a creature had a true effect, that effect would be outside God's power and will, implying the temporal (the creature) overpowers the eternal (God), which is impossible. Hence, no created power has any real causal influence—whether in physical actions (movement, stillness) or moral acts (obedience, disobedience), whether directly or through generated (tawallud) causation.

Key Terms
مثل
تماثل
عجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the argument against two gods, what would happen if they agreed on a single action?
A) They would act together, producing the action jointly.
B) The action cannot be divided, so only one would act, making the other incapable.
C) They would both act, but the action would be duplicated.
D) The action would not occur at all because of disagreement.

Key Takeaway
God's oneness is rationally necessary because multiple gods would lead to mutual incapacity and the non-existence of the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly internalized that only one being has absolute power, how would it change the way you prioritize pleasing Allah over seeking approval from people?
?
Has there been a moment in your life where you felt 'divided' between competing loyalties, as if you were serving multiple masters? How does the rational necessity of God's oneness challenge you to unify your purpose?
?
The argument leads to the conclusion that multiple gods would result in chaos and nothingness. Where in your heart might you be attributing independent power to something other than Allah—like wealth, status, or your own abilities—and how can you actively combat that hidden shirk?

The Denial of Causal Efficacy in Creatures
Sanusi refutes causal efficacy of creatures based on divine unity proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi concludes that no created being has any true causal effect, and the implications of this for human actions and natural events.

Core Idea
If a creature had real power, the temporal would overpower the eternal.

Building on the proof of divine unity, Sanusi extends the reasoning to deny any inherent causal power in creation. This lesson examines the logic and its consequences for understanding divine sovereignty.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text from 'وبهذا الدليل' to the end. Follow the chain of reasoning: from the refutation of polytheism to the denial of creaturely causality.
The phrase 'وبهذا الدليل' ties this argument directly to the previous proof.
2
Trace the logical consequence
The argument claims that if a creature had a real effect, that effect would be outside God's power and will, making the temporal (the creature) predominant over the eternal (God) – an impossibility.
Note the absolute denial: no effect at all, directly or indirectly (tawallud).
3
Apply to everyday examples
Consider actions like moving a hand or choosing to obey. According to Sanusi, these are not caused by our own power but directly by God. Discuss briefly.
This does not negate human responsibility in Islamic theology; it's about the source of causal power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويلزمُ أيضاً : أنْ يكونَ تعالى واحداً في صفاته ؛ بمعنى : أنَّهُ لا مثلَ لهُ ، وإلا لزم الحدوث ؛ لاحتياج كل مِنَ المِثْلَينِ إِلى مَنْ يُخصِّصُهُ بالعارض الذي يمتاز به عن مثله وأيضاً : لو كانَ معَهُ ثانٍ في الأُلُوهِيَّةِ للزمَ أَنْ يكونَ ذلكَ الثاني عام القدرةِ والإرادَةِ مثلَهُ ، وذلكَ يؤدّي إلى اتِّصافِ أحدهما بالعجز ضرورةً ، سواء اختلفا على التضاد ـ وهو ظاهر - أوِ اتَّفقا ؛ لأنَّ الفعل الواحد يستحيل انقسامه ، فلا يمكن أن يقع إلا مِنْ أحدهما ؛ فيلزم عجز الآخر الذي لم يقع منه ، وإذا عجز أحدهما وجب عجز الآخر لتماثلهما ، وذلك يؤدّي إلى ألا يُوجَدَ شيءٌ مِنَ العالم ، والعيانُ يُكذِّبُهُ وبهذا الدليل تعرفُ استحالة أن يكون لشيءٍ مِنَ العالم تأثير البتةَ في أثر ما ؛ لما يلزمُ عليهِ مِنْ خروج ذلك الأثر عن قدرةِ مولانا جلَّ وعزَّ وإرادتِهِ ، وذلكَ يُوجِبُ أنْ يغلبَ الحادث القديم ، وهو محال فلا أثرَ إذاً لقدرةِ المخلوقِ في حركة ولا سكون ، ولا طاعة ولا معصية، ولا في أثر ما على العموم ، لا مباشرةً ولا تولداً
And it also necessarily follows that He, Exalted, is one in His attributes; meaning: that He has no like (mithl), otherwise temporality (huduth) would follow; because each of the two likes would need someone to specify it with the accident by which it is distinguished from its like. Also: if there were a second in divinity with Him, it would necessitate that that second be equal to Him in power and will, and that leads necessarily to one of them being characterized by incapacity ('ajz) — whether they disagree (in which case it is obvious) or they agree; because a single action cannot be divided, so it can only occur from one of them; thus incapacity of the other from whom it did not occur follows, and if one is incapable, the other must be incapable due to their similarity, and that leads to nothing of the world existing, but ocular evidence contradicts this. And by this proof you know the impossibility of anything in the world having any effect whatsoever in any trace; because that would necessitate that trace's departure from the power and will of our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, and that would require the temporal to prevail over the eternal, which is impossible. So there is no effect, therefore, for the power of the created being in any movement or stillness, nor in any obedience or disobedience, nor in any effect at all in general, whether directly or indirectly (tawallud).
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument proving God's oneness in attributes and then drawing a critical conclusion about causality. The author first states that God must be one in His attributes, meaning He has no equal or like. The proof: if there were two likes, each would need a specific cause to distinguish it from the other, which would imply contingency and thus temporality. Then the author provides a sharper proof against polytheism: if there were a second god, it would have to share God's complete power and will. In any scenario—whether the two gods disagree or agree—one of them must be incapable. If they disagree over a contradictory action, only one can act, so the other is incapable. If they agree on a single action, the action cannot be performed by both, so again only one acts. Therefore, one is incapable, and since they are alike, both must be incapable. This leads to the conclusion that nothing in the world would exist, but the observable existence of the world refutes that. The author then says: 'By this proof you know that no created thing has any effect at all.' This is because if a creature had a true effect, that effect would be outside God's power and will, implying the temporal (the creature) overpowers the eternal (God), which is impossible. Hence, no created power has any real causal influence—whether in physical actions (movement, stillness) or moral acts (obedience, disobedience), whether directly or through generated (tawallud) causation.

Key Terms
تأثير
تولد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why can a creature have no real causal effect?
A) Because creatures lack power altogether.
B) Because any real effect would remove that effect from God's power and will, implying the temporal overpowers the eternal.
C) Because creatures only cause effects indirectly through tawallud.
D) Because the world does not exist.

Key Takeaway
No created being has any true causal power; all effects are directly from God, preserving His sole sovereignty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you wake up each day, do you truly believe that your next movement—every step, every gesture—is caused directly by Allah? How would your reliance on Him change if you lived that certainty?
?
Think of a recent sin. In that moment, did you feel your own power was the cause, or did you recognize that even that act was brought into existence by Allah? How can you use this lesson to cultivate deeper humility and repentance?
?
If no creature has any effect, then your 'good deeds' are not truly your own. Does this thought make you feel hopeless or liberated? What does it mean for your gratitude and your fear of Allah?

The Permissibility of Seeing God (Ru'ya) in the Afterlife
Sanusi lists ru'ya among permissible things and proves its possibility by analogy and revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the vision of God (ru'ya) is considered permissible (ja'iz) and how Sanusi proves its possibility by analogy with knowledge and by scriptural testimony.

Core Idea
Seeing God in the afterlife is possible without direction, just as knowing Him is possible without direction.

In this passage, Sanusi turns to a specific example of a permissible action: the vision of God (ru'ya) by believers in the afterlife. This was a debated topic, with some arguing that vision implies direction or corporeality. Sanusi clarifies that just as God creates knowledge in the heart without spatial constraints, He can create sight in the eyes without direction. He then cites revelation as confirmation, making belief in this vision obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Sanusi begins by stating that ru'ya is among the permissible things (ja'izat), and he specifies that it occurs without direction (jihat) or facing (muqabala).
The phrase 'without direction or facing' is crucial for preserving divine transcendence.
2
Understand the analogy between knowledge and sight
Sanusi draws an analogy: just as God creates knowledge ('ilm) in the heart that relates to Him without spatial conditions, He can similarly create sight (basar) in the eyes that relates to Him in a manner befitting His majesty. Reflect on why this analogy works to show possibility.
The key point is that both are perceptions (idrak) that can relate to God without direction.
3
Recognize the role of scriptural testimony
Sanusi concludes by stating that the Law (shar') has informed that this vision will occur for believers in the Hereafter, making faith in it obligatory. This shows that the basis for belief is both rational possibility and revealed confirmation.
Without revelation, the matter would remain merely possible; revelation makes it actual and obligatory to believe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن الجائزات: رؤية المخلوق له تعالى في غير جهة ولا مقابلة؛ إذ كما صح تفضله سبحانه بخلق إدراك لهم في قلوبهم يسمى العلم يتعلق به تعالى على ما هو عليه من غير جهة ولا مقابلة، كذلك يصح تفضله تعالى بخلق إدراك لهم في أعينهم أو في غيرها يسمى ذلك الإدراك البصر يتعلق به تعالى على ما يليق به، وقد أخبر بوقوع ذلك الشرع في حق المؤمنين في الآخرة، فوجب الإيمان به.
And among the permissible things: the vision of the creature of Him, may He be exalted, without direction or facing; for just as His grace, glorified be He, is valid by creating a perception in their hearts called knowledge, which relates to Him, may He be exalted, as He is without direction or facing, similarly it is valid for Him, may He be exalted, to create a perception in their eyes or in other [organs] called that perception 'sight', which relates to Him, may He be exalted, in a manner befitting Him; and the Law has informed that this will occur in the case of the believers in the Hereafter, so faith in it is obligatory.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage provides the example of ru'ya (vision of God) as one of the permissible acts of God. Sanusi first states that the vision occurs without direction (jihat) or facing (muqabala). He then gives an analogy: just as it is valid for God to create a perception (idrak) in the hearts called knowledge ('ilm) that relates to God without spatial conditions, it is similarly valid for Him to create a perception in the eyes (or elsewhere) called sight (basar) that relates to God in a manner befitting His majesty. The argument is that if knowledge of God is possible without direction, sight of God should also be possible since both are perceptions. Finally, Sanusi notes that the Law (shar') has informed believers that vision will occur in the afterlife, therefore affirming it becomes obligatory (wajib al-iman).

Key Terms
الرؤية (al-ru'ya)
العلم (al-ilm)
الإدراك (al-idrak)
الإيمان (al-iman)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that vision of God implies direction or corporeality.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly states that the vision occurs without direction or facing, just like knowledge. Both are perceptions that relate to God without spatial limitations.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Sanusi use to prove the permissibility of seeing God?
A) The way we see physical objects.
B) The way God creates knowledge in the heart without direction.
C) The way angels see God.
D) The way prophets receive revelation.

Key Takeaway
The vision of God in the afterlife is permissible because it is analogous to knowledge of God, both being perceptions without direction, and revelation confirms it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Just as knowledge of God is possible without direction, the vision is possible. If you truly believed that you will see God, would you be more careful about what you look at in this world? What one thing in your daily gaze needs repentance?
?
The Law informs you that believers will see God. Do you live with the certainty that you will be among them? If not, what doubt in your heart needs to be uprooted right now, and what step will you take tonight to strengthen your faith?

The True Nature of Ru'ya: Requirements and Refutations
Sanusi defines ru'ya and refutes misconceptions about obstacles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the essence of ru'ya (vision) according to Ahl al-Haqq, including its single requirement of a locus and the refutation of common misconceptions about physical obstacles.

Core Idea
Ru'ya requires no direction, facing, or rays—only an absolute locus by God's act.

Sanusi clarifies the nature of ru'ya, the vision of Allah, which is a challenge for those who think vision requires physical conditions. He explains that ru'ya is not like ordinary sight; it does not need direction, facing, or any physical medium. This passage establishes the Ash'ari position that vision of God is possible without the usual physical prerequisites, and it refutes false theories about obstacles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the English translation. Note the key terms: ru'ya, mahall, jawhar fard.
Pay attention to the negations: la tastudi'... wa laysat...
2
Identify the positive definition
Sanusi states that ru'ya requires only an absolute locus (mutlaq mahall). No direction, no facing. Understand that this is a theological claim about God's visibility.
The locus is not physical; it's a metaphorical substrate in which the accident of vision subsists.
3
Analyze the refutation of obstacles
Examine the arguments against rays, distance, and veil. Notice that Sanusi shifts the cause of veiling to God's choice, and explains obstacles as accidents in the eye by habit.
This is a kalam explanation using atomistic physics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرؤية عند أهل الحق لا تستدعي بنية ولا جهة ولا مقابلة، وإنما تستدعي مطلق محل تقوم به فقط. وليست بانبعاث أشعة من العين، ولا يمنع منها قرب ولا بعد مفرطان، ولا حجاب كثيف، كما لا يمنع ذلك من العلم. وما تقرر من الموانع في الشاهد فبمحض اختياره تعالى أن يحجب عندها لا بها، وإنما الموانع عند أهل الحق أعراض مضادة للبصر تقوم بجوهر فرد من العين بحسب العادة، وتتعدد بحسب ما فات من المرئيات، كما أن البصر بالنسبة إلينا عرض يقوم بذلك الجوهر الفرد من العين عادة، ويتعدد بعدد ما رئي من المبصرات.
And vision according to the People of Truth does not require any connection nor direction nor facing; rather it only requires an absolute locus in which it subsists. And it is not by the emission of rays from the eye, and neither excessive proximity nor excess distance prevents it, nor a dense veil, just as that does not prevent knowledge. And what is established of obstacles in the witnessed world is by the pure choice of Him, may He be exalted, to veil at them not by them. And the obstacles according to the People of Truth are accidents contrary to sight, subsisting in a single atom of the eye by habit, and they multiply according to what is missed of visible things; just as sight in relation to us is an accident subsisting in that single atom of the eye by habit, and it multiplies by the number of what is seen of visible things.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
In this passage, Sanusi elaborates on the nature of ru'ya according to Ahl al-Haqq (the People of Truth, i.e., the Ash'ari and Maturidi schools). He first states that ru'ya does not require any connection (nisba), direction (jihat), or facing (muqabala); it only needs an absolute locus (mahall) in which it subsists as an accident (arad). He then denies three theories: it is not by emission of rays from the eye (as some philosophers held), and it is not prevented by excessive proximity/distance or a dense veil, because these are physical obstacles that apply to normal sight but not to God's creative act. He then explains that the obstacles (mawani') we observe in the witnessed world (shahid) are not inherently preventing; rather, God by His pure choice creates a veil (hijab) at those occasions but not through them. The true obstacles, according to the People of Truth, are accidents contrary to sight that subsist in a single atom (jawhar fard) of the eye by habit (ada), and they multiply according to the visible objects that are missed. Similarly, sight itself is an accident subsisting in that atom by habit and multiplies by the number of things seen. Thus, all is by God's creation and habit.

Key Terms
الرؤية (al-ru'ya)
أهل الحق (Ahl al-Haqq)
الموانع (al-mawani')
البصر (al-basar)
الجوهر الفرد (al-jawhar al-fard)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that obstacles to vision are natural or physical causes that inherently prevent sight.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that obstacles are accidents created by God's habit, not inherent natural causes. God veils at those occasions by His choice, not through them.

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Haqq as explained by Sanusi, what is required for the vision of God?
A) A direction and facing.
B) An absolute locus without direction.
C) Emission of rays from the eye.
D) The absence of any veil.

Key Takeaway
The essence of ru'ya is that it is an accident created by Allah in a locus, requiring no physical conditions, and all apparent obstacles are by Allah's direct choice, not natural causes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does your current longing to see Allah in the afterlife depend on physical imagination? Will you repent of trying to conceive of Him with spatial limits, and instead yearn for the unconditioned vision described here?
?
If obstacles to seeing Allah are by His pure choice and not by physical causes, why have you been making excuses that 'this world' or 'my distractions' prevent me from knowing Him? What veil are you clinging to by choice?
?
The passage says knowledge is not prevented by distance or veil—do you live as though knowing Allah is that immediate? Or do you let worldly veils convince you that closeness to Allah is impossible? What will you do today to tear down that false belief?

The Reality of Seeing Allah and Refutation of Ray Theory
Sanusi refutes the ray theory of vision and explains the true nature of obstacles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that seeing Allah does not involve physical rays, and that obstacles to vision are solely by Allah's choice, not by natural causes.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah is not physical; obstacles are by divine choice, not natural.

Sanusi continues his discussion on the beatific vision by refuting the theory that vision involves rays emitted from the eye. He clarifies that neither proximity, distance, nor veils prevent Allah from being seen, and that what we consider obstacles are merely occasions for Allah to veil by His pure will. This lesson unpacks Sanusi's argument and his explanation of the true nature of obstacles according to Ahl al-Haqq.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the structure: refutation first, then explanation of obstacles.
2
Identify the main refutation
Sanusi begins by denying that vision involves rays from the eye. Also, he denies that extreme distance, nearness, or a veil can prevent divine vision.
This parallels the impossibility of these preventing knowledge.
3
Understand the role of obstacles
Sanusi explains that what appear as obstacles in this world are not causes in themselves. Allah veils 'on account of them, not by them.' This preserves divine transcendence.
4
Grasp the theory of single substance and habit
True obstacles are attributes contrary to sight that subsist in a single substance (jawhar fard) of the eye by habit. This is a technical Kalam explanation.
This is based on customary causation, not necessary causation.
5
Reflect on divine transcendence
Consider how this explanation removes any physical constraint from Allah's ability to be seen. All is by His will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليسَتْ بانبعاث أشعَةٍ مِنَ العين ، ولا يمنع منها قُرْب ولا بُعد مفرطان ، ولا حجاب كثيف ، كما لا يمنع ذلك مِنَ العلم . وما تقرَّرَ مِنَ الموانع في الشاهد فبمخضِ اختیارِهِ تعالى أن يحجب عندَها لا بها ، وإنَّما الموانع عند أهل الحقِّ أعراض مُضادَّةٌ للبصر تقوم بجوهر فردِ مِنَ العين بحسَبِ العادةِ ، وتتعدَّدُ بحسَبِ ما فاتَ مِنَ المرئيَّاتِ ، كما أنَّ البصرَ بالنسبة إلينا عَرَضٌ يقوم بذلك الجوهر الفردِ مِنَ العينِ عادةً ، ويتعدَّدُ بعددِ ما رُبيَ مِنَ المبصَراتِ
And it is not by the emission of rays from the eye, nor does prevent it extreme proximity or distance, nor a dense veil, just as that does not prevent knowledge. And what has been established of obstacles in the witnessed world is by the pure choice of Him, the Exalted, that He veils on account of them, not by them. And indeed the obstacles according to the people of truth are attributes contrary to sight that subsist in a single substance of the eye according to habit, and they multiply according to what is missed of visible things, just as sight with respect to us is an attribute that subsists in that single substance of the eye habitually, and it multiplies by the number of things seen.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the beatific vision (ru'yah). It refutes the theory that vision is by rays emitted from the eye. Sanusi asserts that extreme nearness, extreme distance, or a dense veil do not prevent Allah from being seen, just as these do not prevent knowledge. He then addresses obstacles to vision: what is established in the witnessed world are not genuine obstacles in themselves, but rather Allah, by His pure choice, causes veiling at the time of these conditions, not by them as causes. The true obstacles, according to Ahl al-Haqq, are attributes that are contrary to sight, which subsist in a single substance (jawhar fard) of the eye by custom ('adah). These obstacles multiply according to the visible objects that are missed. Similarly, sight itself is an attribute that subsists in that single substance by custom, and it multiplies by the number of things seen. This maintains divine transcendence by denying any physical or natural cause for veiling, attributing all to divine will.

Key Terms
الرؤية
البصر
الجوهر الفرد
العادة
الموانع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that seeing Allah requires physical rays or that obstacles like distance or veils naturally prevent vision.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that vision is not by rays, and obstacles are not natural causes; Allah veils by His pure choice on account of them, not by them.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the true reason for obstacles to seeing Allah?
A) Physical conditions like distance or veils.
B) The emission of rays from the eye.
C) Allah's pure choice to veil on account of certain attributes, not by those attributes themselves.
D) The absence of a single substance in the eye.

Key Takeaway
The beatific vision is not physical, and any apparent obstacles are purely by Allah's will, not by natural causes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Praising God with Heart and Tongue
Sanusi enumerates the two modes of praising God and states the necessity of verbal praise for thankfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two modes of praising God—with the heart and with the tongue—and why verbal praise is essential for thankfulness.

Core Idea
Praising God requires both inner conviction and outward verbal acknowledgment.

Sanusi begins by establishing that God is praised in two distinct ways: through the heart's inner recognition of His perfection and through the tongue's verbal confession of His attributes. He then asserts that no act of thankfulness is complete without vocal praise, because the tongue alone can truly express what lies in the heart. This passage lays the foundation for understanding the relation between belief, speech, and gratitude.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two modes of praise
Read the first part of the passage and notice how Sanusi separately mentions praise in the heart and praise with the tongue. Underline the key terms 'القلوب' and 'الألسنة'.
The heart-praise is based on knowledge of Allah's perfection, while tongue-praise is based on verbal acknowledgment.
2
Understand the ranking of praise
Sanusi declares heart-praise as the highest rank. Ask yourself why inner conviction is considered superior to outward expression.
This does not diminish the importance of verbal praise; it highlights the foundation.
3
Grasp the necessity of verbal praise for shukr
Sanusi states that a servant has not thanked Allah if he does not praise Him with his tongue. Reflect on why the tongue is uniquely suited to reveal what is in the heart.
This connects directly to the definition of shukr in the next passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا شك أنَّ مولانا جل وعزَّ مُثْنى عليه بالقلوب ؛ بما عرفتَهُ مِنْ كمال ذاته وصفاتِهِ ، وأَيَّدَتْ ذلكَ العقولُ بالأدلة القاطعة انزاحَتْ عنها عقائدُ الفسادِ التي أنتجها مخص التوهمات والتخيلاتِ وهذا أعظم مراتب الثناء وأفضلُهُ . وهو جلَّ وعلا مُثْنى عليه أيضاً بالألسنةِ ؛ بما تُقِرُّ بِهِ مِن انفرادِهِ تعالى بصفاتِ الجلال والكمال وما اعترفتْ بهِ مِنَ العبودية لهُ والتسليم لأقداره ، والشهادةِ لهُ بالوحدانيَّةِ ، ولا شكَّ أَنَّهُ ما شكرَ اللهَ تعالى عبد لم يحمده بلسانه على ما جاءَ بِهِ الحديثُ (۱) ؛ لأنَّ المنبى عما في الضمير وضعاً والمظهر له حقاً . . هو النطقُ . وحقيقة معنى الشكر : إشاعةُ النعمة والإبانة عنها ، ونقيضُه - وهو (1) منه ما روى البيهقي في شعب الإيمان ( ٤٠٨٥ ) من حديث سيدنا عبد الله بن عمرو رضي الله عنهما مرفوعاً : ( الحمد رأس الشكرِ ، ما شكر الله عبد لا يحمده » ، قال العلامة الطيبي في ( شرح المشكاة » ( ١٨٢٦/٦ ) : ( وإنَّما جعل الحمد رأساً ؛ لأن ذكر النعمة باللسان والثناء على موليها أشيع لها ، وأدلُّ على مكانها من الاعتقاد وآداب الجوارح ؛ لخفاء عمل القلب ، وما في عمل الجوارح من الاحتمال ، بخلاف عمل اللسان ؛ وهو النطق الذي يفصح عن كل خفي، ويجلي عن كل مشتبه ) ، وهو ما سيبينه المصنف في حقيقة معنى الشكر
And there is no doubt that our Lord, Glorious and Exalted, is praised in hearts, by what you have known of the perfection of His essence and attributes, and the intellects have confirmed that with conclusive proofs that dispel the corrupt beliefs produced by pure delusions and illusions. And this is the highest rank of praise and its best. And He, Exalted and Supreme, is also praised with tongues, by what they acknowledge of His exclusivity in attributes of majesty and perfection, and what they confess of servitude to Him, submission to His decrees, and testimony to His oneness. And there is no doubt that a servant has not thanked God if he has not praised Him with his tongue, according to what the hadith has brought; because the tongue is that which, by primal institution, declares what is in the heart and is its true revealer. And the true meaning of thankfulness is the dissemination of the blessing and making it known, and its opposite is—and it is (1) Among it is what al-Bayhaqi narrated in 'Shu'ab al-Iman' (4085) from the hadith of our master Abdullah ibn Amr, may God be pleased with them both, raised to the Prophet: 'Praise is the head of thankfulness: no servant thanks God who does not praise Him.' Al-Tibi said in 'Sharh al-Mishkat' (6/1826): 'He made praise the head because mentioning the blessing with the tongue and praising its bestower makes it more widespread and more indicative of its status than belief and the etiquette of the limbs, due to the concealment of the heart's action and the possibility in the action of the limbs, unlike the action of the tongue, which is speech that reveals every hidden thing and clarifies every ambiguity.' And this is what the author will explain in the true meaning of thankfulness.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage discusses the praise of God with heart and tongue and defines the true meaning of shukr. The author states that God is praised in hearts through knowledge of His perfection, supported by rational proofs that refute corrupt beliefs. This inward praise is the highest form. He is also praised with tongues through verbal acknowledgment of His attributes, servitude, submission, and testimony of His oneness. The author then asserts, based on a hadith, that a person has not thanked God if they have not praised Him with their tongue, because the tongue is the primary means to express what is in the heart. Finally, he defines the true meaning of shukr as disseminating the blessing and making it known, implying its opposite is concealment. The footnote provides the hadith and a commentary by al-Tibi explaining why praise with the tongue is considered the head of thankfulness due to its clarity and power to spread the blessing.

القلوب
الألسنة

A) Praising with the tongue
B) Praising in the heart

D) Neither, only actions matter

Key Takeaway
God is praised both inwardly through knowledge and outwardly through speech, and verbal praise is indispensable for true thankfulness.

?
