Iblis's Error: Attributing Effect to Self
Sanusi presents the Sunni denial of other effective agents and then narrates Iblis's error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fundamental error of Iblis—attributing his own actions and excellence to himself—and the Sunni rejection of any effective agent other than God.

Core Idea
Iblis's sin was not just disobedience but attributing his own actions to himself.

Sanusi begins by restating the Sunni position: no other effective agent exists besides God. He then uses Iblis as a case study to show how the false belief in one's own efficacy leads to arrogance and rebellion. This lesson examines the two hidden ignorances in Iblis that caused his downfall.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Sunni framework
Recognize that Ahl al-Sunnah affirm no effective agent but God; read the opening lines of the passage.
The key term 'مؤثر' (effective agent) is central.
2
Identify Iblis's two ignorances
Note the two 'جهالتين' (ignorances) in Iblis: (1) considering himself superior due to origin, (2) seeing himself as the doer of his own worship.
3
See how these led to his statements
Read how Iblis openly declared 'I am better than him' and accused God of injustice.
His words reflect the two ignorances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا جريان لها على مذهب أهل السنة المتبرئينَ مِنَ الحولِ والقوَّةِ ، والمفوضين جميع الأمور إلى الله تعالى ، لا يرونَ معَهُ جل وعزَّ شريكاً في ملكه، ولا مؤثراً سواه في أثرٍ ما على العموم، لا بطبعه ولا بخاصية جُعِلَتْ فيهِ. ولأجلِ كُمون هاتين الجهالتين في باطن إبليس ، وانطواء عقدِهِ عليهما لما خلق الله آدمَ عليهِ السلامُ مِنَ التراب ، وهو المفضولُ عندَ إبليس اللعين بالنسبة إلى النار التي خُلِقَ هو منها ، ثم أُمِرَ في جملة الملائكة بالسجودِ لآدمَ والتعظيمِ لقَدْرِهِ ، ولم تتقدَّمْ مِنْ آدمَ عليهِ السلامُ عبادةٌ . . أَنفَ إبليس - لعنَهُ اللهُ - وعظم أصله وعبادته ؛ إذ رأى نفسَه فاعلاً لها ، وَجوَّرَ مولانا جل وعزّ في حُكمِهِ عليهِ بالسجودِ لآدمَ عليه السلام والتواضع له (۱)، وجاهرَهُ عزَّ وجلَّ بقولِهِ : أَنَا خَيْرٌ مِنْهُ [الأعراف : ۱۲] ، وبقوله : أَرَعَيْنَكَ هَذَا الَّذِي كَرَّمْتَ عَلَيَّ [الإسراء : ٦٢] ! وانظر الفرقَ بينَ هذا اللعينِ ، وبين الملائكةِ الكرام عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام ؛ فإنَّهم خُلِقوا مِنْ عظيم النور ، وعبدوا الله تعالى قبل أن يُوجَدَ إبليس اللعين آلافاً مِنَ السنينَ ، ثم معَ ذلك عندما أمرهم مولانا جل وعزّ بالسجودِ لآدمَ عليهِ السلامُ .. بادروا كلُّهم لامتثال أمرِهِ سبحانه ، مُتلذذينَ بطاعتِهِ تعالى في ذلك ، خائفين منه سبحانه مغتنمينَ عظيم رضاه جلَّ وعزَّ ، حامدينَ لهُ بأعظم المحامدِ مِنْ حيثُ أمَّلَهم لخطاب تكليفِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ (۱)، ولم يلتفتوا إلى النور الذي هو أصلهم ؛ إذ هو وغيره سواءٌ . واختصاصُهُ بما اختص بهِ إِنَّما هو بمخض فضل الله تعالى ، لا بطبعه ، فروا عليهم السلامُ أنَّ ذلكَ ممَّا يُوجِبُ غرقهم في بحارِ أَنْعُمِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ ؛ إِذْ حَصَّهم مِنَ النِّعَمِ الجليلة بلا استحقاق منهم لشيء منها عليه تعالى بما لم يعطِهِ غيرَهم ، وهو القادر سبحانَهُ أنْ يجعلَ الترابَ مضيئاً ونوراً ، ويجعل النور مظلماً. وكذا لم يلتفتوا أيضاً عليهم السلام إلى ما مضى منهم مِنْ عظيمِ العبادة ؛ إذ هي فعْلُ اللهِ تعالى بلا واسطةٍ ، فلم يرَوا لأنفسهم تأثيراً ألبتةَ ، فهم وآدمُ عليهِ السلامُ في عدم إيجاد شيء مِنَ العبادة سواء ، ولهذا قال تعالى مادحاً لهم بما وفقهم له سبحانَهُ مِنْ حُسْنِ الاعتقادِ والامتثال بمحْضِ فضلِهِ : ﴿ فَسَجَدَ الْمَلَائِكَةُ كُلُّهُمْ أَجْمَعُونَ ﴾ [صَ : ٧٣] ، فوَكَّدَ تعالى تعميم السجودِ في جميعهم بـ ( كل ) و ( أجمع ) بعد ما أتى بصيغة العموم في قوله : ﴿ الْمَلَائِكَةُ ﴾ ، دَفْعاً لما يُستغربَ مِنْ وقوع السجودِ مِنْ جميعهم مع كثرتهم جداً كثرةً تخرج عن الحصر. عسى أنْ والله سبحانه وتعالى يتفضَّلُ على مَنْ شاءَ بالكرامة العظمى ؛ وهي كرامة الاستقامة في الظاهر والباطن ، ويعدلُ فيمَنْ شَاءَ؛ فيحتُّمُ عليهِ
And it has no application according to the school of Ahl al-Sunnah, who disavow power and strength, and who entrust all affairs to God Almighty, not seeing with Him, may He be glorified and exalted, any partner in His dominion, nor any other effective agent in any effect whatsoever, neither by its nature nor by a property placed in it. And because of the concealment of these two ignorances in the inner self of Iblis, and the tying of his knot upon them, when God created Adam, peace be upon him, from dust—and he was inferior according to the accursed Iblis compared to the fire from which he himself was created—then he was commanded along with the angels to prostrate to Adam and to magnify his rank, while no worship had preceded from Adam, peace be upon him, Iblis—may God curse him—became disdainful, and magnified his own origin and worship, because he saw himself as the doer of it, and he attributed injustice to our Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, in His command to him to prostrate to Adam, peace be upon him, and to humble himself before him, and he openly said to Him, may He be glorified and exalted: 'I am better than him' [al-A'raf: 12], and by His saying: 'Do You see this one whom You have honored above me?' [al-Isra': 62]! And consider the difference between this accursed one and the noble angels, peace and blessings be upon them: for they were created from great light, and they worshipped God Almighty thousands of years before the accursed Iblis existed. Then, despite that, when our Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, commanded them to prostrate to Adam, peace be upon him, they all hastened to obey His command, taking pleasure in His obedience in that, fearing Him, may He be exalted, seizing His great pleasure, may He be glorified and exalted, praising Him with the greatest praise because He made them hopeful of the address of His obligation, may He be glorified and exalted (1), and they did not pay attention to the light which was their origin, for it and other things are equal. And their being distinguished by what they were distinguished by is solely by the pure grace of God Almighty, not by their nature. For they fled, peace be upon them, from that which would cause them to drown in the seas of His blessings, may He be glorified and exalted, because He granted them great blessings without any deserving from them of anything from Him, to the extent that He did not give to others. And He is able, may He be glorified, to make dust luminous and light, and to make light dark. Likewise, they also did not pay attention, peace be upon them, to what had passed from them of great worship, for it is the act of God Almighty without intermediary. So they did not see for themselves any effect at all. Thus they and Adam, peace be upon him, are equal in not bringing into existence any worship. Therefore, God Almighty said, praising them for what He had granted them success for, by His pure grace, of good belief and obedience: 'So the angels prostrated, all of them together' [Sad: 73]. So He emphasized the generalization of prostration among all of them with 'all' and 'entirely' after He had come with a formula of generality in His saying: 'the angels', to repel what might be wondered at of the occurrence of prostration from all of them, despite their being extremely numerous, too numerous to count. Perhaps that, and God, may He be exalted, bestows upon whom He wills the greatest honor, which is the honor of uprightness in outward and inward, and He is just toward whom He wills; so He necessitates upon him.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument contrasting the erroneous belief of Iblis (Satan) with the correct belief of the angels, as an illustration of the Sunni creed regarding divine action and human agency. The author begins by restating the position of Ahl al-Sunnah: they disavow any inherent power or strength (حول وقوة) and entrust all affairs to God, seeing no partner with Him and no other effective agent (مؤثر) in any effect, whether by nature or by a property placed in it. This sets the framework for understanding the error of Iblis. Iblis had two hidden ignorances (جهالتين) in his inner self: first, he considered himself superior because he was created from fire while Adam was from dust; second, he saw himself as the doer (فاعلاً) of his own worship and excellence. When commanded to prostrate to Adam, he became arrogant, magnified his own origin and worship, and even attributed injustice (جور) to God for commanding him to humble himself before a being with no prior worship. He openly declared his defiance using Qur'anic verses. The author then contrasts Iblis with the noble angels. They were created from great light and had worshipped God for thousands of years before Iblis existed. Yet when commanded to prostrate, they hastened to obey, taking pleasure in obedience, fearing God, and hoping for His reward. They did not rely on their noble origin (light), recognizing that it and other things are equal in that they are created. Their distinction (اختصاص) is purely by God's grace (فضل), not by their nature. They fled from any sense of entitlement, realizing that even their worship is God's act without intermediary (بلا واسطة). Thus they saw themselves as having no effect (تأثير) whatsoever, being equal to Adam in not bringing worship into existence. God praised them for this correct belief and obedience, emphasizing in the verse 'So the angels prostrated, all of them together' with multiple words of generalization to dispel any wonder that all of them prostrated despite their vast numbers. The passage ends with a supplication and the author's hope that God bestows the honor of uprightness and is just to whom He wills.

Key Terms
حول وقوة
مؤثر
جور
فاعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Iblis's sin was simply arrogance, not a theological mistake about causality.
Correction: The passage shows his arrogance was rooted in the false belief that he was the independent doer of his own actions, which is a theological error about agency.

Checkpoint
What did Iblis attribute to himself that led to his rebellion?
A) His creation from fire
B) His worship and excellence as his own doing
C) His long years of worship
D) His knowledge

Key Takeaway
Iblis's error was attributing his own actions to himself, neglecting that all efficacy belongs to God alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something good, do you ever secretly feel that it was due to your own effort or merit, instead of seeing it entirely from God? When was the last time you caught yourself thinking 'I did this' rather than 'God enabled this'? How will you train yourself to immediately attribute every success back to Him starting today?
?
The passage says Iblis magnified his own worship and origin. Are you prone to boasting about your religious deeds—your prayers, charity, or knowledge—as if they make you superior to others? Imagine standing before Allah tomorrow: would He hold you accountable for seeing yourself as the source of your own piety?
?
Iblis's hidden ignorance led him to accuse God of injustice. Have you ever questioned God's decree in your life—perhaps when something didn't go your way—and felt He was unfair? What specific event comes to mind, and how will you replace that thought with the conviction that He alone is the effective agent and never does injustice?

The Angels' Correct Creed: All Actions Are from God
Sanusi contrasts the angels' humility and correct attribution of all actions to God with Iblis's self-attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the angels' recognition that their worship and excellence are purely from God's grace, not from their own nature or effort.

Core Idea
The angels saw no effect from themselves; even their worship was God's act.

After contrasting Iblis, Sanusi presents the noble angels as the embodiment of correct belief. Despite their high rank and long worship, they attributed all to God and obeyed immediately. This lesson explores their humility and doctrinal correctness.

Guided Path
1
Consider the angels' high status
Note they were created from light and worshipped for thousands of years before Adam.
This makes their humility even more striking.
2
See their response to God's command
They hastened to obey with pleasure and fear, not relying on their origin.
3
Understand why they saw no effect from themselves
They recognized that their distinction and worship are purely by God's grace, not by their own doing.
Key term: 'بلا واسطة' (without intermediary).

ولا جريان لها على مذهب أهل السنة المتبرئينَ مِنَ الحولِ والقوَّةِ ، والمفوضين جميع الأمور إلى الله تعالى ، لا يرونَ معَهُ جل وعزَّ شريكاً في ملكه، ولا مؤثراً سواه في أثرٍ ما على العموم، لا بطبعه ولا بخاصية جُعِلَتْ فيهِ. ولأجلِ كُمون هاتين الجهالتين في باطن إبليس ، وانطواء عقدِهِ عليهما لما خلق الله آدمَ عليهِ السلامُ مِنَ التراب ، وهو المفضولُ عندَ إبليس اللعين بالنسبة إلى النار التي خُلِقَ هو منها ، ثم أُمِرَ في جملة الملائكة بالسجودِ لآدمَ والتعظيمِ لقَدْرِهِ ، ولم تتقدَّمْ مِنْ آدمَ عليهِ السلامُ عبادةٌ . . أَنفَ إبليس - لعنَهُ اللهُ - وعظم أصله وعبادته ؛ إذ رأى نفسَه فاعلاً لها ، وَجوَّرَ مولانا جل وعزّ في حُكمِهِ عليهِ بالسجودِ لآدمَ عليه السلام والتواضع له (۱)، وجاهرَهُ عزَّ وجلَّ بقولِهِ : أَنَا خَيْرٌ مِنْهُ [الأعراف : ۱۲] ، وبقوله : أَرَعَيْنَكَ هَذَا الَّذِي كَرَّمْتَ عَلَيَّ [الإسراء : ٦٢] ! وانظر الفرقَ بينَ هذا اللعينِ ، وبين الملائكةِ الكرام عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام ؛ فإنَّهم خُلِقوا مِنْ عظيم النور ، وعبدوا الله تعالى قبل أن يُوجَدَ إبليس اللعين آلافاً مِنَ السنينَ ، ثم معَ ذلك عندما أمرهم مولانا جل وعزّ بالسجودِ لآدمَ عليهِ السلامُ .. بادروا كلُّهم لامتثال أمرِهِ سبحانه ، مُتلذذينَ بطاعتِهِ تعالى في ذلك ، خائفين منه سبحانه مغتنمينَ عظيم رضاه جلَّ وعزَّ ، حامدينَ لهُ بأعظم المحامدِ مِنْ حيثُ أمَّلَهم لخطاب تكليفِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ (۱)، ولم يلتفتوا إلى النور الذي هو أصلهم ؛ إذ هو وغيره سواءٌ . واختصاصُهُ بما اختص بهِ إِنَّما هو بمخض فضل الله تعالى ، لا بطبعه ، فروا عليهم السلامُ أنَّ ذلكَ ممَّا يُوجِبُ غرقهم في بحارِ أَنْعُمِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ ؛ إِذْ حَصَّهم مِنَ النِّعَمِ الجليلة بلا استحقاق منهم لشيء منها عليه تعالى بما لم يعطِهِ غيرَهم ، وهو القادر سبحانَهُ أنْ يجعلَ الترابَ مضيئاً ونوراً ، ويجعل النور مظلماً. وكذا لم يلتفتوا أيضاً عليهم السلام إلى ما مضى منهم مِنْ عظيمِ العبادة ؛ إذ هي فعْلُ اللهِ تعالى بلا واسطةٍ ، فلم يرَوا لأنفسهم تأثيراً ألبتةَ ، فهم وآدمُ عليهِ السلامُ في عدم إيجاد شيء مِنَ العبادة سواء ، ولهذا قال تعالى مادحاً لهم بما وفقهم له سبحانَهُ مِنْ حُسْنِ الاعتقادِ والامتثال بمحْضِ فضلِهِ : ﴿ فَسَجَدَ الْمَلَائِكَةُ كُلُّهُمْ أَجْمَعُونَ ﴾ [صَ : ٧٣] ، فوَكَّدَ تعالى تعميم السجودِ في جميعهم بـ ( كل ) و ( أجمع ) بعد ما أتى بصيغة العموم في قوله : ﴿ الْمَلَائِكَةُ ﴾ ، دَفْعاً لما يُستغربَ مِنْ وقوع السجودِ مِنْ جميعهم مع كثرتهم جداً كثرةً تخرج عن الحصر. عسى أنْ والله سبحانه وتعالى يتفضَّلُ على مَنْ شاءَ بالكرامة العظمى ؛ وهي كرامة الاستقامة في الظاهر والباطن ، ويعدلُ فيمَنْ شَاءَ؛ فيحتُّمُ عليهِ
And it has no application according to the school of Ahl al-Sunnah, who disavow power and strength, and who entrust all affairs to God Almighty, not seeing with Him, may He be glorified and exalted, any partner in His dominion, nor any other effective agent in any effect whatsoever, neither by its nature nor by a property placed in it. And because of the concealment of these two ignorances in the inner self of Iblis, and the tying of his knot upon them, when God created Adam, peace be upon him, from dust—and he was inferior according to the accursed Iblis compared to the fire from which he himself was created—then he was commanded along with the angels to prostrate to Adam and to magnify his rank, while no worship had preceded from Adam, peace be upon him, Iblis—may God curse him—became disdainful, and magnified his own origin and worship, because he saw himself as the doer of it, and he attributed injustice to our Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, in His command to him to prostrate to Adam, peace be upon him, and to humble himself before him, and he openly said to Him, may He be glorified and exalted: 'I am better than him' [al-A'raf: 12], and by His saying: 'Do You see this one whom You have honored above me?' [al-Isra': 62]! And consider the difference between this accursed one and the noble angels, peace and blessings be upon them: for they were created from great light, and they worshipped God Almighty thousands of years before the accursed Iblis existed. Then, despite that, when our Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, commanded them to prostrate to Adam, peace be upon him, they all hastened to obey His command, taking pleasure in His obedience in that, fearing Him, may He be exalted, seizing His great pleasure, may He be glorified and exalted, praising Him with the greatest praise because He made them hopeful of the address of His obligation, may He be glorified and exalted (1), and they did not pay attention to the light which was their origin, for it and other things are equal. And their being distinguished by what they were distinguished by is solely by the pure grace of God Almighty, not by their nature. For they fled, peace be upon them, from that which would cause them to drown in the seas of His blessings, may He be glorified and exalted, because He granted them great blessings without any deserving from them of anything from Him, to the extent that He did not give to others. And He is able, may He be glorified, to make dust luminous and light, and to make light dark. Likewise, they also did not pay attention, peace be upon them, to what had passed from them of great worship, for it is the act of God Almighty without intermediary. So they did not see for themselves any effect at all. Thus they and Adam, peace be upon him, are equal in not bringing into existence any worship. Therefore, God Almighty said, praising them for what He had granted them success for, by His pure grace, of good belief and obedience: 'So the angels prostrated, all of them together' [Sad: 73]. So He emphasized the generalization of prostration among all of them with 'all' and 'entirely' after He had come with a formula of generality in His saying: 'the angels', to repel what might be wondered at of the occurrence of prostration from all of them, despite their being extremely numerous, too numerous to count. Perhaps that, and God, may He be exalted, bestows upon whom He wills the greatest honor, which is the honor of uprightness in outward and inward, and He is just toward whom He wills; so He necessitates upon him.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument contrasting the erroneous belief of Iblis (Satan) with the correct belief of the angels, as an illustration of the Sunni creed regarding divine action and human agency. The author begins by restating the position of Ahl al-Sunnah: they disavow any inherent power or strength (حول وقوة) and entrust all affairs to God, seeing no partner with Him and no other effective agent (مؤثر) in any effect, whether by nature or by a property placed in it. This sets the framework for understanding the error of Iblis. Iblis had two hidden ignorances (جهالتين) in his inner self: first, he considered himself superior because he was created from fire while Adam was from dust; second, he saw himself as the doer (فاعلاً) of his own worship and excellence. When commanded to prostrate to Adam, he became arrogant, magnified his own origin and worship, and even attributed injustice (جور) to God for commanding him to humble himself before a being with no prior worship. He openly declared his defiance using Qur'anic verses. The author then contrasts Iblis with the noble angels. They were created from great light and had worshipped God for thousands of years before Iblis existed. Yet when commanded to prostrate, they hastened to obey, taking pleasure in obedience, fearing God, and hoping for His reward. They did not rely on their noble origin (light), recognizing that it and other things are equal in that they are created. Their distinction (اختصاص) is purely by God's grace (فضل), not by their nature. They fled from any sense of entitlement, realizing that even their worship is God's act without intermediary (بلا واسطة). Thus they saw themselves as having no effect (تأثير) whatsoever, being equal to Adam in not bringing worship into existence. God praised them for this correct belief and obedience, emphasizing in the verse 'So the angels prostrated, all of them together' with multiple words of generalization to dispel any wonder that all of them prostrated despite their vast numbers. The passage ends with a supplication and the author's hope that God bestows the honor of uprightness and is just to whom He wills.

Key Terms
فضل
تأثير
بلا واسطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The angels deserved praise because of their long worship and high origin.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that they were praised for recognizing that all is from God's grace and that they saw no effect from themselves.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the angels not rely on their origin of light?
A) Because they forgot it
B) Because they considered it equal to other things and recognized distinction is by God's grace
C) Because they were created from fire
D) Because they were commanded not to

Key Takeaway
The angels' correct creed is to see no effect from themselves and to attribute all to God's grace.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you ever feel a sense of pride or self-satisfaction? The angels, despite their long worship and noble origin, saw no effect from themselves. How can you train yourself to see your own obedience as purely from God's grace, and what would change in your heart if you did?
?
You were created with talents and opportunities. The lesson teaches that any distinction is solely by God's grace, not by your nature. Is there any area of your life where you secretly believe you deserve credit? What would it mean for you to abandon that belief?
?
The angels did not look back at their past worship; they saw it as God's act. When you reflect on your past acts of worship, do you see them as your achievements or as God's favor? How does this perspective affect your humility and reliance on God?

Metaphorical Interpretation of Anthropomorphic Expressions
Sanusi explains metaphorical interpretations of 'hand' and 'eye' in Quranic verses to avoid literalism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets Quranic anthropomorphic expressions metaphorically to uphold divine transcendence.

Core Idea
Anthropomorphic verses are understood metaphorically to protect God's transcendence.

Sanusi now turns to specific Quranic verses that seem to attribute human body parts to God. He shows that these must be understood metaphorically, not literally. This lesson examines his interpretations of 'hand' and 'eye' and the four possible meanings of 'eyes' in the verse about Noah's ark.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle for 'hands'
Read how Sanusi explains that if 'hands' is taken metaphorically, it refers to power, and the dual form is used for magnification.
This sets the method: metaphorical interpretation avoids literalism.
2
Interpretation of 'eye' in Surah Ta-Ha
Find the two interpretations: knowledge or protection/preservation.
3
Four interpretations of 'Our eyes'
List the four possible meanings for 'eyes' in Al-Qamar 14: knowledge, protection, springs of water, and leaders/nobles.
The fourth is incomplete but still instructive.
4
Notice the method
Observe that Sanusi offers multiple valid interpretations, all avoiding anthropomorphism.
This reflects the richness of Quranic exegesis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا كلُّهُ إِنْ فهمنا التثنية في اليدين على الحقيقة ، وأما إنْ فهمناها على المجاز ، وأنَّ المراد بها إنَّما هو القدرة .. فإنَّما تُثَنَّى القدرة وإنْ كانَتْ واحدةً لتعظيمها بالتثنية ؛ كما يُعظَّم الشيء الواحد بالتعبير عنه بالجمع . وأما ( العينُ ) في قولِهِ : ﴿ وَلِتُصْنَعَ عَلَى عَيْنِي ﴾ [طه : ٣٩] : فأُوِّلَتْ بالعلم ، أو بالكلاءة والحفظ ، وكذلك قوله تعالى : ﴿ تَجْرِى بِأَعْيُنِنَا ﴾ [القمر : ١٤] ، وهذه الآية تحتمل أربعة أوجه مِنَ التأويل : أحدها : ما ذكرناهُ مِنَ العلم . الثاني : مِنَ الكلاءةِ والرعاية ، ويكون التكثير بالجمع راجعاً إلى تعظيم العلم أو تعظيم الكلاءةِ . ويحتمل أن يكونَ التكثيرُ راجعاً إلى كلاءةِ اللهِ تعالى كلَّ مَنْ في السفينة ؛ إذْ يكلا الله تعالى كلَّ واحدٍ منهم بكلاءة تخصه . ويحتمل أن تكونَ الكثرةُ في ذلكَ باعتبار الكلاءةِ مِنَ اللهِ سبحانَهُ ، ومِنَ الملائكةِ ؛ بمعنى : أنَّهُ سبحانَهُ يأمرهم بصحبة أهل السفينة ومؤانستهم في تلك الغمَراتِ . الثالث : يحتمل أن يكون المراد بـ ( الأعين ) أعين الماء التي تفجَّرَتْ ؛ كقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَفَجَّرْنَا الْأَرْضَ عُيُونًا ﴾ [القمر : ١٢] ، قيل : كانَ الماء ينزلُ مِنَ السماءِ ويخرجُ مِنَ الأرضِ ، فلا يتركُ النازلُ مِنَ السماءِ الخارج مِنَ الأرض أن يصعد ، ولا يتركُ الخارجُ مِنَ الأرضِ النازِلَ مِنَ السماءِ أن يصل إلى الأرضِ ، فَالْتَقَى الْمَاءُ عَلَى أَمْرٍ قَدْ قُدِرَ ﴾ [القمر : ١٢] ، وقد قيل : إن جميع الأرض كان يخرج منها الماء ، وإنَّ الماء كان ينزلُ مِنْ أبواب السماء المتّسعة . الرابع : يحتمل أن يكون معنى قوله تعالى : ﴿ تَجْرِى بِأَعْيُنِنَا ﴾ [القمر : ١٤] : تجري بساداتِ أهل الأرض ، وأعين الناس ساداتهم وخيارهم، ولما لم يكن على وجْهِ الأَرضِ مِنْ بني آدمَ في ذلك الوقتِ مؤمن إلا [؟]
And all this if we understand the dual in 'the hands' literally, but if we understand it metaphorically, and that what is meant by it is only power... then power is expressed in the dual even though it is one, to magnify it through the dual; just as a single thing is magnified by expressing it in the plural. As for 'the eye' in His statement: {And that you be made under My eye} [Ta-Ha: 39]: it is interpreted as knowledge, or as protection and preservation. Similarly, His statement, Exalted: {Sailing under Our eyes} [Al-Qamar: 14]. And this verse admits four aspects of interpretation: One: what we mentioned of knowledge. Second: of protection and care, and the pluralization (multiplicity) goes back to magnifying the knowledge or magnifying the protection. And it is possible that the pluralization goes back to Allah's protection of everyone in the ship, as Allah protects each one of them with a protection specific to him. And it is possible that the multiplicity in that is in consideration of the protection from Allah, Glorified, and from the angels, meaning that He, Glorified, commands them (the angels) to accompany the people of the ship and keep them company in those distresses. Third: it is possible that what is meant by 'the eyes' is the springs of water that gushed forth, as His statement, Exalted: {And We caused the earth to gush forth springs} [Al-Qamar: 12]. It is said: The water descended from the sky and came out from the earth, and the descending from the sky did not let the coming out from the earth ascend, and the coming out from the earth did not let the descending from the sky reach the earth, so the water met on a matter which had been decreed. And it is said: All the earth was bringing forth water, and the water was descending from the wide gates of the sky. Fourth: it is possible that the meaning of His statement, Exalted: {Sailing under Our eyes} [Al-Qamar: 14] is: sailing with the leaders of the people of the earth, and 'eyes' of the people are their leaders and nobles. And since there was no believer on the face of the earth from the children of Adam at that time except [؟]
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a hermeneutical discussion on how to interpret anthropomorphic expressions in the Quran, specifically 'hand' (يد) and 'eye' (عين). The author begins by noting that if we understand the dual form in 'hands' literally, that is one way, but if we understand it metaphorically (مجاز), then the intended meaning is 'power' (قدرة). The dual form is used to magnify the power, just as the plural is used to magnify a single thing. He then turns to the word 'eye' in the verse from Surah Ta-Ha 39: 'that you be made under My eye.' This is interpreted either as 'knowledge' (علم) or 'protection and preservation' (كلاءة وحفظ). Similarly, the verse from Surah Al-Qamar 14: 'Sailing under Our eyes' admits four possible interpretations. The first is knowledge. The second is protection and care, with the plural form serving to magnify either the knowledge or the protection; it may also indicate protection for each individual in the ship, or protection from both Allah and the angels. The third interpretation takes 'eyes' literally as the 'springs of water' that gushed forth, referring to the flood, and he describes how the water from the sky and the earth met. The fourth interpretation, which is cut off, suggests that 'eyes' means the 'leaders and nobles' of the people, and that the ship sailed with them, noting that at that time there were no believers on earth except... (the text breaks off). The author thus demonstrates the richness of Quranic interpretation and the rejection of crude anthropomorphism.

Key Terms
تأويل
مجاز
يد
عين
كلاءة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That anthropomorphic verses must be taken literally without allowance for metaphorical interpretation, leading to anthropomorphism (tashbih).
Correction: Sanusi shows that these verses admit multiple metaphorical interpretations, all of which avoid attributing physical body parts to Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many possible interpretations does the verse 'Sailing under Our eyes' (Al-Qamar 14) have?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Quranic anthropomorphic expressions must be understood metaphorically to maintain God's transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever pictured God with human-like attributes when reading verses like 'the hand of God'? How does this lesson challenge you to actively purify your mental image of God? What practical step will you take today to ensure you think of God as transcendent, beyond any physical form?
?
Sanusi provides multiple valid interpretations for a single verse. Are you willing to accept that your own understanding of God's attributes may be incomplete? How can you cultivate intellectual humility in matters of faith, especially when discussing these verses with others?
?
If you were asked by someone why you don't take Quranic descriptions of God literally, could you clearly explain the principle of metaphorical interpretation using this lesson? What is at stake for your iman if you neglect to defend God's transcendence in such conversations?

Three Interpretations of 'Kullu Shay'in Halikun illa Wajhahu'
Sanusi lists three opinions on the meaning of 'illa wajhahu' in Surah al-Qasas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three distinct interpretations of the Quranic phrase 'illa wajhahu' and how they relate to divine transcendence and sincere action.

Core Idea
The verse 'Everything perishes except His Face' has layered meanings: literal death, ontological passing away, and moral fruitlessness.

Sanusi presents three scholarly opinions on the meaning of a famous Quranic verse. These interpretations range from literal to metaphorical, each offering a unique perspective on what it means for something to be 'perishing' and for Allah to be eternal. Before we examine the specific interpretations, it is helpful to note that the verse itself is often cited in discussions of tawhid and the nature of Allah's exclusivity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the three opinions.
Pay attention to the key term 'halik' and how it is understood differently.
2
Understand the first interpretation
The first interpretation takes 'halik' as 'dead' (mayyit), meaning every living thing dies except Allah. This is a literal reading based on Quranic usage.
Notice the author's use of another verse to support this meaning.
3
Understand the second interpretation
The second interpretation sees 'halik' as 'passing away' (fanin) from its essence, meaning everything other than Allah is contingent and subject to annihilation, while Allah is preeternal and everlasting.
This interpretation emphasizes ontological dependency.
4
Understand the third interpretation
The third interpretation is moral: 'halik' means 'fruitless' or 'without benefit'. Actions done for other than Allah are worthless, while those done sincerely for His face have lasting reward.
The author connects this to the following verse about judgment and return.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider how these three interpretations together protect divine transcendence and encourage sincere worship. Which one resonates most with you?
Each interpretation highlights a different aspect of tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله تعالى : ﴿ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ هَالِكُ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُ ﴾ [القصص : ۸۸] ففي معناه ثلاثة أقوال : أحدها : أنْ يكونَ ( هالكٌ ( بمعنى : ميت ؛ كقوله تعالى : إِنْ امْرُؤٌ هَلَكَ أي : ماتَ ، فتقديرُ الآية : كلُّ حي ميت إلا الله تعالى الثاني : كُلُّ شَيْءٍ هَالِكُ ﴾ أي : فانٍ مِنْ حيث ذاتُهُ إلا الله سبحانه ؛ فإِنَّهُ واجب القدمِ والبقاء الثالثُ : المعنى : كلُّ ما فُعِلَ لغير الله تعالى فإِنَّهُ هالك ؛ أي : لا فائدة فيه ولا ثمرة له ، إلا ما فُعِلَ لوجهِ اللهِ تعالى ؛ أَي : قُصِدَ بهِ امتثال أمره ، فإنَّهُ لا تنقطعُ فائدتُهُ ، ولذلك قال في سياق الآية : ﴿لَهُ الْحُكْمُ وَإِلَيْهِ تُرْجَعُونَ ﴾ [القصص : ۸۸] أي: له الحكم بالتكليف ، وإليه المرجعُ في إعطاء الثوابِ لمَنْ أخلص لهُ العملَ جلَّ وعزَّ .
As for His statement, Exalted is He: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' [al-Qasas 28:88], there are three sayings about its meaning: One: that 'halik' means dead, like His statement: 'If a man perishes (halaka)' i.e., dies. So the estimation of the verse is: every living thing dies except Allah. The second: 'Everything is perishing' i.e., passing away from its essence except Allah, Glorified be He; for He is necessarily preeternal and everlasting. The third: the meaning is: everything done for other than Allah is perishing, i.e., there is no benefit in it and no fruit, except what is done for the Face of Allah, i.e., intended by it to obey His command, for its benefit does not cease. That is why He said in the context of the verse: 'His is the judgment, and to Him you will be returned' [al-Qasas 28:88], i.e., His is the judgment by obligation, and the return is to Him for giving reward to whoever is sincere in his work for Him, Glorified be He and Exalted.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of three interpretations of the Quranic verse 'Kullu shay'in halikun illa wajhahu' (Everything is perishing except His Face). The author presents them as three distinct sayings (aqwal). The first interpretation takes 'halik' in the sense of 'dead' (mayyit), drawing on the usage in the Quran where 'halaka' means 'died'. Under this view, the verse means: every living thing dies except Allah. The second interpretation takes 'halik' as 'passing away' (fanin) from its essence, meaning that everything other than Allah is contingent and subject to annihilation, while Allah alone is necessarily preeternal and everlasting. The third interpretation is more metaphorical: 'halik' means 'fruitless' or 'without benefit', so the verse means that any action performed for other than Allah is worthless, whereas actions performed sincerely for Allah's face (i.e., seeking His pleasure) have lasting reward. The author supports this third opinion by noting the following verse: 'His is the judgment, and to Him you will be returned', indicating that judgment and return are for the purpose of reward for sincere deeds. Thus, the passage provides three possible understandings of the same phrase, each with its own nuance: literal death, ontological contingency, and moral futility.

Key Terms
الهلاك
الفناء
الإخلاص
وجه الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think 'illa wajhahu' refers to a physical face of Allah, implying anthropomorphism.
Correction: The three interpretations show that 'wajhahu' can mean 'except Allah Himself' (first two) or 'except what is done for His sake' (third), avoiding any literal anthropomorphic reading.

Checkpoint
Which interpretation of 'illa wajhahu' relates to the benefit of actions?
A) The first: everything dies except Allah.
B) The second: everything perishes in essence except Allah.
C) The third: everything done for other than Allah is fruitless.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'illa wajhahu' in Surah al-Qasas has been interpreted in three ways: literal death, essential passing away, and moral fruitlessness, each highlighting a different aspect of Allah's transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the third interpretation is correct, that actions done for other than Allah are fruitless, examine your own daily deeds—how many of them are truly done for Allah's face? What would you need to change to ensure your efforts are not 'perishing'?
?
The second interpretation says everything other than Allah is perishing from its essence. What attachments in your life—people, possessions, status—are you holding onto as if they will last? How does this belief reshape your priorities starting today?
?
The first interpretation reminds you of death. If you knew you would die within a year, which of your current actions would you consider wasted? What is one concrete step you can take this week to align your life more with the third interpretation, seeking Allah's reward above all?

First Proof: Impossibility of Temporal Attributes in Eternity
Sanusi presents a reductio proof against temporal attributes in pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that an attribute cannot be both in pre-eternity and temporally posterior, as it would involve a contradiction between necessity and contingency.

Core Idea
A single attribute cannot be both necessary and contingent — that is a reversal of reality.

Sanusi now presents the first of his proofs for divine transcendence. Using a reductio ad absurdum, he shows that if an attribute were to exist in pre-eternity (al-azal) and also be temporally posterior, it would have to be both necessary and contingent — an impossible contradiction. This argument relies on the established distinction between the necessary (wājib) and the contingent (jā'iz). Let's follow his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully, noticing the structure of the proof. Then read the literal translation.
Pay attention to the words 'واجبة' and 'جائزة'.
2
Identify the two implications
The proof rests on two implications: existence in pre-eternity makes an attribute necessary; temporal posteriority makes it contingent. Identify these two claims in the text.
3
Understand the contradiction
The author argues that combining these two possibilities for the same attribute is a 'tanāquḍ lā yu'qal' — an unintelligible contradiction. See why this is a 'reversal of realities'.
Think about what it means to treat the necessary as contingent and vice versa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اتصافه بصفة كذا في الأزلِ .. ينافي صحة تأخُرِ تلك الصفة عنِ الأزلِ ؛ لما فيهِ مِنْ قلب الحقائقِ (١) ؛ لأنَّ صحة وجودِ الصفة في الأزلِ يستلزمُ كونها واجبةً ؛ لما بيَّنَّاهُ فيما سبق ، وصحةَ تأخُرِها عنِ الأزلِ يستلزمُ كونها جائزةً ، وقد سبق بيانه أيضاً ، فالجمع بينهما تناقض لا يُعقَلُ ، وقلبٌ للحقيقةِ ؛ بجعل الواجب جائزاً ، والجائز واجباً • فعليك بهذا التحقيق في هذا المقام ؛ فإِنَّهُ مِنْ مَزال الأقدامِ ، ولن تجدَ - والله أعلمُ - مَنْ كشف القناعَ عن وجْهِ هذا البرهان كما كشفناه نحنُ ، والله تعالى الحمدُ ، وبه التوفيقُ ، لا ربَّ غيرُه .
His being described with a certain attribute in pre-eternity contradicts the validity of that attribute being temporally posterior to pre-eternity; because of the reversal of realities (1). For the validity of the attribute's existence in pre-eternity necessitates that it be necessary (wājib), as we have explained previously, and the validity of its being temporally posterior to pre-eternity necessitates that it be contingent (jā'iz), as its explanation has also preceded. Thus combining them is an unintelligible contradiction and a reversal of reality, by making the necessary contingent and the contingent necessary. So hold fast to this verification in this station; for it is a slippery slope. And you will not find—and God knows best—anyone who has unveiled the face of this proof as we have unveiled it. And all praise is due to God Almighty, and from Him is success; there is no lord other than Him.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof (al-burhān al-awwal) that it is impossible for God to be described with a temporal (ḥādith) attribute in pre-eternity (al-azal). The proof is structured as a reductio ad absurdum: if we suppose that it is valid for God to have a certain attribute in pre-eternity, then that attribute must be necessary (wājib) because whatever exists in pre-eternity without beginning is necessary. But if we also suppose that the same attribute could be temporally posterior to pre-eternity (i.e., come into existence later), then it would be contingent (jā'iz), because what is temporally posterior can be absent and is not necessary. Combining these two possibilities—that the attribute is both necessary and contingent—is a logical contradiction (tanāquḍ lā yu'qal) and a reversal of reality (qalb al-ḥaqīqa), because it treats the necessary as contingent and the contingent as necessary. The author then emphasizes the importance of this verification, warning that this point is a slippery slope where many slip. He claims originality in unveiling this proof and ends with praise to God.

Key Terms
الأزلِ (al-azal)
الواجب (al-wājib)
الجائز (al-jā'iz)
تناقض (tanāquḍ)
قلب الحقائق (qalb al-ḥaqā'iq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think an attribute could be necessary in one sense and contingent in another, allowing it to be both in pre-eternity and later.
Correction: The proof shows that the same attribute cannot have both modal statuses simultaneously; it is either necessary (if pre-eternal) or contingent (if temporal), not both.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, why is it impossible for an attribute to be both in pre-eternity and temporally posterior?
A) Because it would require the attribute to be both necessary and contingent, which is a contradiction.
B) Because God cannot have attributes at all.
C) Because temporal attributes are impossible by definition.
D) Because the attribute would have to be created by God.

Key Takeaway
It is impossible for an attribute to be both necessary (from pre-eternity) and contingent (temporally posterior) because that is a logical contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's attributes, do you ever unconsciously imagine them as changing or developing over time, like human qualities? How does this proof challenge that mental image?
?
This proof shows that combining necessity and contingency in God's attributes is a contradiction. In your own understanding of God, are there any comfortable but contradictory beliefs you hold about His nature? What would it cost you to let them go?
?
Sanusi warns that this point is a 'slippery slope where many slip.' Have you ever slipped into thinking that God's knowledge or power could have come into being after not existing? What difference would it make in your worship if you truly believed His attributes are eternal and unchanging?

The Second Proof: Uniformity of Acceptance and Impossibility of Temporal Attributes
Sanusi presents the second proof of the impossibility of temporal attributes in God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of Sanusi's second proof that God cannot have any temporal attribute, because such an attribute would lead to God's temporality.

Core Idea
Acceptance of attributes is an invariant self-property, so one temporal attribute would make God temporal.

This lesson presents Sanusi's second argument against the possibility of temporal attributes in God. The proof builds on the principle that an essence's capacity to receive attributes is a fixed property that does not vary. Sanusi shows that if God could receive a temporal attribute, He would necessarily be described with it or its opposite, both of which are temporal, thereby entailing His own temporality—which is impossible given His established pre-eternity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the argument. Notice the logical flow and key terms.
The passage is dense; reading it twice may help.
2
Identify the key premise
The proof begins by stating that acceptance of attributes is a self-property (ṣifa nafsiyya) that does not vary. This is the foundation of the argument.
A self-property is intrinsic and unchanging.
3
Trace the entailment
Follow how the proof moves from the invariance of acceptance to the necessity of all accepted attributes, using God's known essential attributes as examples.
If God must have knowledge, power, will, and life, then any other attribute He accepts must also be necessary.
4
Understand the contradiction
The argument assumes a temporal attribute, shows that it would force God to be temporal, which contradicts His known pre-eternity. This shows the assumption is impossible.
Temporality (ḥudūth) means being originated, while pre-eternity (qidam) means without beginning.
5
Reflect on the overall proof
Consider how this proof strengthens the doctrine of divine transcendence by ruling out temporal attributes in God's essence.
This is one of several proofs for the same conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان الثاني ] وأيضاً : لوِ اتَّصفَ تعالى بصفةٍ حادثة لم يجز أنْ يَعرى عنها ، أو عن ضدها ، أو عن مثلها ، وإلا لجاز عروه عن جميع الصفاتِ ؛ لأنَّ قبوله لها ذاتي لا يختلف(٢) ، وقد عرفْتَ فيما سبق استحالةَ عروِّهِ عن العلم والقدرةِ والإرادة والحياة • فثبت : أَنَّ كلَّ ما يقبلُهُ مِنَ الصفاتِ لا يعرى عنه إلا للاتّصافِ بضدّهِ أو مثلِهِ (١) ، لكنَّ ضدَّ تلك الصفة الحادثة أو مثلَها لا يكون إلا حادثاً ؛ بدليل طريانِ عدمِهِ ؛ إذ القديم لا ينعدم ، وما لا يعرى عن الحوادث يكون حادثاً ضرورةً ، فلزمَ أَنَّهُ لوِ اتَّصفَ تعالى بصفة حادثة لوجب حدوثه ضرورةً ، وقد عرفت وجوبَ قدمِهِ جلَّ وعلا • هذا هو البرهان الثاني على استحالة قيام الحوادث بذاتِهِ تعالى وتقريرُهُ أَنْ يُقالَ : لوِ اتَّصفَ تعالى بصفة حادثة للزم حدوثه ، ذلك علوّاً كبيراً ، وبيانُ اللزومِ في ذلكَ : أَنَّ القبول قد تقرَّرَ أنَّهُ صفةٌ نفسيَّةُ للقابل ، فيلزمُ ألا يختلف ، فإذا ما وجبَ لبعض الصفاتِ التي تقبلها ذات أيُّ ذات كانَتْ يجب لسائرِ تلك الصفاتِ • وقد تقرَّرَ بالبرهان القاطعِ : الوجوبُ لصفات تقبلها ذات مولانا جلَّ وعزَّ ؛ وهي العلم والقدرة والإرادة والحياة ، وأن تجرد الذات العليَّةِ عن هذهِ الصفاتِ مستحيل عقلاً ، فكذا يجب إذا للذات العليَّةِ كلُّ صفةٍ تقبلها ، وعرؤُها عن تلك الصفة مستحيل • فإذا عرفت هذا فنقولُ : لو فُرِضَ اتصافُهُ تعالى بصفةٍ حادثة .. لزمَ أنْ تكونَ ذاتُهُ جَلَّ وعزَّ قابلة لتلك الصفة ، أو لضدها ، أو مثلها (١) في هامش ( هـ ، ج ) نسخة : ( إلا لاتصف ) بدل ( للاتصاف )
The Second Proof. Also: If the Exalted were described with a temporal attribute, it would not be permissible for Him to be free from it, or from its opposite, or from its like; otherwise it would be permissible for Him to be free from all attributes, because His acceptance of them is a self-property that does not vary (2). And you already know the impossibility of His being free from knowledge, power, will, and life. So it is established: every attribute that He accepts, He is not free from it except by being described with its opposite or its like (1). But the opposite of that temporal attribute or its like is only temporal, by the evidence of the advent of its non-existence; for the eternal does not become non-existent, and whatever is not free from temporal things is necessarily temporal. Hence it follows that if the Exalted were described with a temporal attribute, His temporality would be necessary, and you already know the necessity of His pre-eternity, may He be exalted. This is the second proof of the impossibility of temporal accidents subsisting in His essence, and its elucidation is to say: If the Exalted were described with a temporal attribute, His temporality would follow—highly exalted is He above that. The explanation of the entailment is: Acceptance has been established as a self-property of the acceptor, so it necessarily does not vary. Thus, if it is necessary for some of the attributes that a certain essence accepts, it must be necessary for all of those attributes. And it has been established by decisive proof: the necessity for attributes that the essence of our Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, accepts—namely knowledge, power, will, and life—and that the supreme essence's being divested of these attributes is intellectually impossible. So likewise, it must be necessary for the supreme essence every attribute it accepts, and its being divested of that attribute is impossible. Thus, if you know this, we say: If it were supposed that the Exalted is described with a temporal attribute, then it would follow that His essence, may He be glorified and exalted, would be receptive to that attribute, or to its opposite, or to its like.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof (al-burhān al-thānī) that temporal attributes cannot subsist in God's essence. The argument proceeds as follows: (1) Acceptance of attributes is a self-property (ṣifa nafsiyya) of the subject, which does not vary. (2) It has already been established that God necessarily possesses certain essential attributes (knowledge, power, will, life) and cannot be divested of them. (3) Therefore, if God accepts any attribute, He must accept it necessarily, and cannot be free from it except by having its opposite or like. (4) If a temporal attribute were accepted, its opposite or like would also be temporal (since the eternal does not become non-existent). (5) Consequently, God would necessarily be described with that temporal attribute or its opposite/like, making Him composite of temporal accidents, which entails His temporality (ḥudūth). (6) But God's pre-eternity (qidam) is already established, so the assumption is impossible. The author then restates the proof more formally: acceptance is uniform; since God necessarily has certain attributes, He must necessarily have all attributes He accepts; so if He accepted a temporal attribute, He would necessarily have it, leading to temporality. The margin notes a variant reading.

Key Terms
صفة حادثة (ṣifa ḥāditha)
الذاتي (al-dhātī)
القديم (al-qadīm)
الحدوث (al-ḥudūth)
البرهان القاطع (al-burhān al-qāṭi')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Acceptance of attributes can vary depending on the attribute; God might accept some attributes necessarily and others optionally.
Correction: Acceptance is a self-property of the essence, which is uniform. If God necessarily accepts some attributes (like knowledge), then He must necessarily accept any attribute He is capable of accepting. The proof shows that acceptance does not vary.

Checkpoint
According to the second proof, what would follow if God could accept a temporal attribute?
A) He would necessarily accept all temporal attributes, leading to His temporality.
B) He would be free from all attributes.
C) He would become composite of eternal and temporal.
D) He would require a creator.

Key Takeaway
The uniformity of acceptance forces any attribute accepted by God to be necessary, so a temporal attribute would entail God's temporality, which is impossible given His pre-eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If acceptance of attributes is an invariant self-property in God, what does that demand from you regarding your own acceptance of His commands? Are you consistent in submitting to every area of His law, or do you pick and choose, thereby attributing a varying 'acceptance' to your Lord?
?
Sanusi proves that describing Allah with a temporal attribute would entail His temporality. But do you, in your heart, sometimes imagine Allah's attributes changing—like His anger subsiding after you repent as if He were affected by time? How does this proof compel you to purify your understanding of Allah's eternity and perfection?
?
This proof rests on the principle that what is not free from temporals is itself temporal. Your soul is constantly subject to temporal thoughts and emotions—does that not serve as a stark reminder of your own contingency and need for the Eternal One? How will you live today with the certainty that only Allah is free from change?

Third Proof: Temporal Attributes Imply Deficiency
Sanusi presents the third proof against temporal attributes in God's essence with a two-case analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third rational proof for why temporal attributes cannot subsist in God's essence, and how the two-case analysis demonstrates the impossibility.

Core Idea
A temporal attribute, whether perfection or deficiency, implies deficiency in God's essence.

This lesson presents the third proof from Sanusi's Umm al-Barahin against the possibility of temporal accidents in God's essence. The proof works by considering two cases: if the attribute is a deficiency, it is clearly impossible; if it is a perfection, its absence in pre-eternity would be a deficiency. By analyzing both possibilities, Sanusi demonstrates the logical necessity of God's transcendence from temporal change.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to understand the author's argument.
Notice the compact style of Sanusi's reasoning.
2
Identify the two cases
The proof splits into two possibilities: the temporal attribute is either a deficiency or a perfection. Find where these are stated.
The first case is mentioned but not elaborated; the second is explained in detail.
3
Understand why each case leads to deficiency
For the first case, the conclusion is obvious. For the second, consider why absence in pre-eternity constitutes deficiency.
Reflect on the phrase 'Fawt al-kamal naqs' (absence of perfection is deficiency).
4
Note the author's focus on the hidden case
Sanusi explains that he only elaborates on the second case because the deficiency there is less obvious. Understand why he does this.
This is a common pedagogical technique in kalam.
5
Reflect on the overall conclusion
The proof shows that any temporal attribute would entail deficiency, which is impossible for God. Conclude that God cannot have temporal accidents.
This ties back to the doctrine of divine transcendence (tanzih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ البرهان الثالث ] وأيضاً : فهو جلَّ وعزَّ لا يتّصفُ إلا بالكمال إجماعاً فيلزمُ في هذه الصفة الحادثة التي فُرِضَ اتصافُهُ تعالى بها أن تكونَ مِنْ صفاتِ الكمال ، وقد فاتَتْ ذاته العليَّةَ في الأزل ؛ لفَرْضِ حدوثها ، وفوتُ الكمال نقص ، وهو تعالى مُنزَّه عنه بإجماع العقلاء . هذا هو البرهان الثالثُ على استحالة قيام الحوادث بذاتِهِ العليَّةِ وتقريرهُ أنْ يُقالَ : لوِ اتَّصفَ تعالى بصفة حادثة لزمَ اتِّصافُهُ تعالى بالنقائص ، تعالى الله عن ذلكَ علوّاً كبيراً . وبيانُ الملازمة في ذلكَ : أنَّ تلك الصفة الحادثة التي فُرِضَ اتِّصافُهُ تعالى بها : إما أن تكون صفة نقص ، وإِمَّا أَنْ تكون صفة كمال فإنْ كانَتْ صفةَ نقص : فلزوم اتصافه تعالى بالنقص على تقدير اتّصافِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ بتلك الصفةِ الحادثة . . واضح البطلان . وإنْ كانَتْ صفةَ كمالٍ : لزمَ لفَرْضِ حدوثها ألا تكون ثابتة للذاتِ العليَّةِ في الأزلِ ؛ لمنافاة الحدوثِ للأزلِ ، فلزمَ إذاً أن تكونَ الذاتُ العليَّةُ ناقصة في الأزلِ ؛ لفواتِ هذهِ الصفات الكاملة لها ؛ إذ لا خفاءَ أنَّ فوتَ الكمال نقص . فقد بان لك بهذا : أنَّ اتصافَهُ تعالى بصفة حادثة يستلزم اتصافَهُ جل وعز بصفة نقص ، سواء قدَّرْتَ أنَّ تلك الصفة الحادثة صفةٌ نقص ، أو قدَّرْتَ أنَّها صفةٌ كمال . ولمَّا كانَ لزوم النقص على التقديرِ الأَوَّلِ جليّاً ، وعلى الثاني خفياً .. أضربنا في أصل العقيدة عن التقدير الأوَّلِ لوضوح لزومِ النقص معَهُ ، واقتصرنا على بيان الثاني لخفائه . فقوله : ( وقد فاتَتْ ذاتَهُ العليَّةَ في الأزلِ ) أي : أنَّ تلك الصفةَ الحادثة وإنْ كانَتْ صفة كمالٍ يلزمُ أنْ تفوت الذات في الأزلِ ؛ أي : لا تكون ثابتة لها فيهِ ؛ لاستحالة كون الحادثِ قديماً
[The third proof] And also: He, the Mighty and Majestic, does not qualify except with perfection by consensus, so it necessitates in this temporal attribute which it is assumed that He is qualified with, that it be among the attributes of perfection, and it has passed from His lofty essence in pre-eternity due to the assumption of its temporality, and the absence of perfection is deficiency, and He is exalted above it by consensus of the rational people. This is the third proof upon the impossibility of the subsistence of temporal accidents in His lofty essence, and its explanation is that it is said: If He, exalted, is qualified with a temporal attribute, it necessitates that He is qualified with deficiencies—far exalted is Allah above that tremendously. And the explanation of the implication in that: that temporal attribute which it is assumed He is qualified with: either it is an attribute of deficiency, or it is an attribute of perfection. If it is an attribute of deficiency, then the necessity of His being qualified with deficiency upon the assumption of His being qualified with that temporal attribute is clearly false. And if it is an attribute of perfection, then due to the assumption of its temporality, it necessitates that it is not established for the lofty essence in pre-eternity, because temporality contradicts pre-eternity. So it necessitates then that the lofty essence be deficient in pre-eternity due to the absence of these perfect attributes from it, since it is not hidden that the absence of perfection is deficiency. So it has become clear to you by this: that His being qualified with a temporal attribute necessitates His being qualified with deficiency, whether you consider that temporal attribute to be an attribute of deficiency or you consider it an attribute of perfection. And since the necessity of deficiency upon the first estimation is clear, and upon the second is hidden... we passed over in the foundation of creed the first estimation due to the clarity of the necessity of deficiency with it, and we limited ourselves to explaining the second due to its hiddenness. So His saying: 'And it has passed from His lofty essence in pre-eternity' means that that temporal attribute even if it is an attribute of perfection, it necessarily passes from the essence in pre-eternity; i.e., it is not established for Him in it, due to the impossibility of the temporal being eternal.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof against the possibility of temporal attributes subsisting in God's essence. The proof begins by stating that God is qualified only with perfection by consensus. Therefore, any assumed temporal attribute must be a perfection. However, because it is temporal, it would have been absent from God in pre-eternity, implying a deficiency—since lacking perfection is deficiency. This is impossible. The proof then analyzes two possibilities: whether the attribute is a deficiency or a perfection. If deficiency, the impossibility is clear. If perfection, its absence in pre-eternity entails deficiency in God before acquiring it, which is also impossible. The author notes that he only elaborated on the second case because it is less obvious. Finally, he clarifies the phrase 'it has passed from His lofty essence in pre-eternity' to mean the attribute is not established for God in pre-eternity, because a temporal thing cannot be eternal.

Key Terms
صفة حادثة
صفة كمال
صفة نقص
الأزل
فوت الكمال
الذات العليَّة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think a temporal attribute of perfection does not imply deficiency if it is later acquired, because the perfection is eventually present.
Correction: The proof shows that the absence of the attribute in pre-eternity itself is a deficiency, regardless of later acquisition. God's essence must be perfect at all times, including pre-eternity.

Checkpoint
According to the third proof, if God were qualified with a temporal attribute that is a perfection, what would necessarily follow?
A) It would prove God's omnipotence.
B) The attribute would have been absent in pre-eternity, implying deficiency.
C) The attribute would be eternal.
D) It would be a deficiency rather than perfection.

Key Takeaway
Any temporal attribute in God would necessitate deficiency, which is impossible, so God is free from temporal accidents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If any deficiency in God is impossible, then your trust in Him should be absolute. In what area of your life do you find yourself doubting that God's plan for you is perfect? What will you do today to surrender that doubt to His perfect will?
?
The proof shows that even the absence of a perfection in God would be a deficiency. Does your concept of God ever reduce Him to something less than absolutely perfect? How will you actively guard your thoughts to ensure you never attribute imperfection to Him?
?
Since God lacks nothing, your own neediness before Him is total. Are there moments when you act as if you are self-sufficient, forgetting that every perfection you have comes from Him? What concrete change will you make this week to remind yourself of your complete dependence on the Perfect One?

Refuting the Objection of Successive Perfections
Sanusi refutes an objection about successive perfections without a first.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the objection that God could be qualified with an infinite succession of temporal attributes without a first, by showing it leads to an impossible infinite regress.

Core Idea
Infinite succession without a first is impossible; it's sheer regress.

Sanusi now addresses a subtle objection to the third proof. One might argue that even if a specific temporal attribute wasn't present in pre-eternity, God could still be perfect by being qualified with similar perfections in an endless chain without a first. This objection attempts to avoid the conclusion that God lacked perfection. Sanusi's refutation is brief but powerful, resting on the impossibility of an infinite regress of temporal events. Pay careful attention to how he dismantles this possibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection presented
The objector claims that the third proof does not necessitate deficiency because God might be qualified with similar perfections in succession without a first.
This is a classic objection to arguments from contingency or perfection.
2
Identify Sanusi's direct refutation
Sanusi declares the possibility false and gives the reason: it would be an infinite regress (tasalsul) of temporal events with no beginning.
He uses the phrase 'حوادث لا أول لها' (temporal events without a first).
3
Understand why this regress is impossible
In kalam, actual infinites and infinite regresses of temporal events are considered impossible because they entail contradictions and absurdities.
This is a foundational principle in Islamic theology.
4
Review the key terms
Familiarize yourself with the terms: اعتراض (objection), احتمال (possibility), اتصاف بأمثالها (being qualified with likes), التسلسل (infinite regress), حوادث لا أول لها (temporal events without a first).
These terms are crucial for understanding kalam argumentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يُعترَضُ على هذا : بأنَّه لا يلزم منه فوتُ الذاتِ العليَّة كمال هذه الصفة الحادثة (۱) ؛ لاحتمال اتصافه بأمثالها على التوالي لا إلى أوَّلِ ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : لا يخفى أنَّ هذا الاحتمال باطل ; لأنَّهُ تسلسلٌ مِنْ بابِ حوادث لا أَوَّلَ لها وهو ظاهر الاستحالة
And do not object to this: that it does not necessitate from it the absence from the lofty essence of the perfection of this temporal attribute, due to the possibility of His being qualified with its likes in succession without a first; because we say: it is not hidden that this possibility is false, because it is an infinite regress from the category of temporal events that have no first, and it is manifestly impossible.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage addresses a possible objection to the third proof. The objector suggests that even if a specific temporal attribute is not present in pre-eternity, God could still be perfect by being qualified with similar perfections successively, without any first instance. This would avoid the conclusion that God lacked perfection at any point. The author rejects this by pointing out that such a succession would constitute an infinite regress of temporal events, which is impossible. Therefore, the objection is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An infinite chain of past events is possible.
Correction: Kalam holds that actual infinites and infinite regress of temporal events are impossible because they entail logical absurdities.

Key Takeaway

Proof of Divine Oneness by Negating Composition
Sanusi proves divine oneness by negating composition and clarifies its meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for God's oneness by negating composition, and the refutation of the misconception that this implies an indivisible atom.

Core Idea
Composition would make God a body or multiple gods—therefore He is one and indivisible.

Sanusi presents a logical argument for tawḥīd by focusing on the impossibility of composition in the divine essence. He shows that composition leads to absurdities, and then clarifies what negating composition truly means, guarding against the misconception that God is an indivisible atom. The reasoning is foundational for understanding divine simplicity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Get a feel for the flow of the argument.
2
Identify the two consequences of composition
Notice that if God were composed of parts, either each part would be divine (leading to multiple gods) or only some parts would be divine (requiring a specifier, implying contingency). Both are impossible.
This is the core of the proof.
3
Understand the clarification
Sanusi emphasizes that negating composition does not mean God is an indivisible atom, because that would still be a body. Rather, it means He has no size at all.
This prevents a common misunderstanding.
4
Reflect on the importance
Consider why this argument is essential: it establishes God's transcendence beyond physical categories and affirms His unique oneness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفي الكموم المستحيلة عنه سبحانه ] ويلزمُ أنْ يكونَ تعالى واحداً في ذاتِهِ ؛ بمعنى : أَنَّهُ غيرُ مُركَّب ، وإلا لزمَ أنْ يكونَ جسماً ، وأيضاً : فلو تركَّبَ مِنْ جزأين فأكثر لم يخلُ : إما أن يقوم بكل جزء صفات الألوهية، أو يختص قيامها بالبعض ، والأَوَّلُ يلزم منه تعدُّدُ الآلهة والثاني يلزم منه الحدوث ؛ للاحتياج إلى المخصص بعضها بصفاتِ الأُلوهِيَّةِ ؛ لاستواء جميعها في قبولِ تلك الصفاتِ وليس معنى نفي التركيب في الذاتِ العليَّةِ أنَّها جزء لا يتجزأ ، وإلا لزمَ أنْ تكون جوهراً فرداً ، وقد سبق استحالةُ الجرْميَّةِ عليهِ مطلقاً (۱) ، وإنَّما المقصود : أنَّ الذات العليَّةَ لا تقبلُ صِغَراً ولا كِبَراً ؛ لأنَّهما مِنْ عوارض الأجرام ، وهو تعالى يستحيل أن يكون جرماً .
Negation of the impossible relative to Him, Exalted. It follows that He, Exalted, must be one in His essence, meaning that He is not composed, otherwise He would be a body. Also, if He were composed of two or more parts, then it would inevitably be either that the attributes of divinity reside in every part, or their residence is specific to some. The first entails multiplicity of gods, and the second entails contingency due to the need for a specifier to specify some of them with the attributes of divinity, since all are equal in capacity to receive those attributes. And the meaning of negating composition in the Supreme Essence is not that it is an indivisible part, otherwise it would be an individual atom, and it has already preceded that corporeality is absolutely impossible for Him. Rather, the intended meaning is that the Supreme Essence does not accept smallness or bigness, because they are accidents of bodies, and He, Exalted, is impossible to be a body.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage contains a proof for the unity of the divine essence by negating composition. The author begins by stating that God must be one in essence, meaning not composed. He provides two arguments: first, composition would make Him a body, which is impossible. Second, if He were composed of two or more parts, either each part would possess divine attributes, leading to multiple gods, or only some parts would possess them, requiring a specifier and thus contingency. The author then clarifies that negating composition does not mean God is an indivisible atom (which is also a body), but rather that He is free from size, which is an accident of bodies. The argument follows a logical structure: assuming composition leads to absurdities (taʿaddud al-āliha or ḥudūth), therefore composition is impossible.

Key Terms
وحدانية الذات
تركيب
جسم
جزء
جوهر فرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Negating composition implies God is an indivisible atom (jawhar fard).
Correction: An indivisible atom is still a body with size, which is impossible for God. Negation of composition means God has no parts and no dimensions whatsoever.

Checkpoint
What is the second argument given against composition of the divine essence?
A) It would require a body.
B) It would lead to either multiple gods or contingency.
C) It would imply an indivisible atom.
D) It would entail change.

Key Takeaway
God's oneness is proven by negating composition, and this negation does not mean He is an atom but that He is beyond size and body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The proof shows that if God were composed, He would need a specifier—making Him dependent on something else. As you examine your daily trust, are there ways you treat God as if He is composed—needing conditions or parts to act? Clarifying the Negation of Composition in God
Sanusi corrects a misconception about negation of composition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct meaning of negating composition from God, and why it does not imply smallness or atomism.

Core Idea
Negating composition in God does not mean He is like an atom; it means He is beyond size.

Sanusi warns against a subtle misunderstanding: that negating composition makes God like an indivisible atom, implying extreme smallness. He corrects this by stating that God does not accept smallness or bigness because these are properties of bodies, and God is utterly unlike bodies. This lesson unpacks that clarification.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall point.
Notice the structure: purpose, misconception, correction, and conclusion.
2
Identify the misconception being corrected
What does Sanusi say people might imagine when they hear 'negation of composition'? Find the phrase about the indivisible atom (jawhar fard).
The misconception is that God becomes like an atom—extremely small.
3
Understand the positive meaning
Sanusi clarifies that God is self-subsisting but not a 'meaning among meanings' and does not accept smallness or bigness. Relate this to God's difference from bodies.
This connects to the broader principle of God's incomparability to creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وليس معنى نفي التركيب ... ) إلى آخره : إنَّما ذكر هذا الكلام دفعاً لما يُتوهَّمُ مِنْ أنَّ المراد بنفي التركيب في ذاته تعالى التناهي في الدقةِ كما هو معنى نفي التركيب في الجوهر الفردِ ، فنبَّهَ على أنَّ المراد ليس ذلكَ ، وإِنَّما المرادُ أنَّ ذاتَهُ تعالى - وإِنْ كانَ قائماً بنفسِهِ - ليس بمعنى مِنَ المعاني ، فهو معَ ذلك لا يقبلُ صِغَراً ولا كِبَراً ؛ لأنَّهما مِنْ خواص الأجرام ، وهو تعالى مباين للأجرام وصفاتها على ما تقرَّرَ في فصلِ وجوب مخالفته تعالى للحوادث (۱) والعجز بعد هذا عن الإدراك إدرال (۲) ، ولا يعرفُ الله على الكمال إلا الله (۳) ، وبالله تعالى التوفيقُ ، لا ربَّ غيره ، ولا معبود سواه .
His saying: ('And the meaning of negation of composition is not...') to its end: He only mentioned this statement to ward off what might be imagined that the intended meaning of the negation of composition in His essence, Exalted is He, is [that He is] extremely small (al-tanahi fi al-diqqa) as is the meaning of the negation of composition in the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). So he alerted that the intended meaning is not that. Rather, the intended meaning is that His essence, Exalted is He — even though it is self-subsisting — is not a meaning among meanings; yet with that, it does not accept smallness or bigness, because they are properties of bodies (ajram), and He, Exalted is He, is utterly different (mubayin) from bodies and their attributes as established in the chapter on the necessity of His being different from contingents (al-hawadith) (1). And incapacity after this to perceive is perception (2), and none knows God perfectly except God (3). And with God Most High is success; there is no lord other than Him, and no worshipped other than Him.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a clarification (tanbih) regarding the correct understanding of negating composition from God. The author warns against a common misinterpretation: that negating composition means God is like an indivisible atom (jawhar fard), which implies extreme smallness. Instead, the negation means that God does not accept smallness or bigness at all, because these are properties of bodies (ajram). God is utterly unlike bodies and their attributes. The author then concludes by stating that true knowledge of God is recognizing one's incapacity to fully comprehend Him, and that only God knows Himself perfectly.

Key Terms
نفي التركيب (nafy al-tarkib)
جوهر فرد (jawhar fard)
أجرام (ajram)
مخالفة للحوادث (mukhalafa lil-hawadith)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Negating composition means God is like an indivisible atom (jawhar fard) — extremely small and point-like.
Correction: Negating composition means God is not composed of parts and is not subject to smallness or bigness; these are properties of bodies, and God is unlike bodies.
