The Proof of God's Exclusive Creation
Proof of exclusive creation via impossible outcomes of dual power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that only God has the attribute of creating and effecting, by considering the impossibility of two powers producing opposite effects on the same thing.

Core Idea
Only Allah creates and effects; any other power is ineffective.

The commentator begins by presenting a hypothetical scenario: if divine power and created power were both attached to opposite effects on the same body at the same time, several impossible outcomes would result. This proves that created power cannot truly produce any effect and that exclusive creation belongs to Allah alone. Let us examine the proof step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the hypothetical scenario
Read the Arabic passage carefully. The commentator assumes divine power attached to movement of a body and created power attached to stillness of the same body at the same time.
This sets up a conflict to test whether both powers can be truly effective.
2
Analyze the three possible outcomes
Work through each of the three logical possibilities: both effects occur, neither occurs, or only one occurs. Notice how each leads to an impossibility (conjunction of opposites, divine incapacity, or preference without a preferrer).
The third outcome is the critical one: if only one occurs, either God is incapacitated or there is arbitrary preference.
3
Grasp the conclusion
The only consistent conclusion is that created power has no real effect; all creation is exclusively from Allah. Read the sentence starting with 'فبان لك بهذا' to see the conclusion.
The attribute of 'effect ing and creating' is a special characteristic of Allah alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأَمَّا إِنْ قُدِّرَ اختلافُهما - كأن نفرض تعلُّق قدرةِ المولى جل وعزَّ وإرادته بحركة جسم في زمان كذا ، وتعلق قدرة الغير بسكون ذلكَ الجسمِ في ذلك الزمانِ المعيَّنِ - فحينئذٍ نقولُ : لا يخلو :
إما أن يقع الأمران جميعاً ، فيلزم عليه اجتماع الضدين وهما الحركة والسكون
أو لا يقعَ واحد منهما ، فيلزم عجز الباري تعالى عن ذلكَ ، ويلزم أيضاً عُرُو ذلكَ الجِرْمِ عن الحركة والسكون
أو يقع أحدهما دونَ الآخرِ ، فإنْ كانَ ذلكَ الواقع هو مقدور الغيرِ لزم تعجيزُ الإله جلَّ وعزَّ ، وإنْ كانَ الواقع مقدور المولى جل وعزَّ لزم الترجيحُ بلا مُرجُحٍ ، ولزم أيضاً جواز عجزِ القدرة القديمة ؛ لفَرْضِ مساواتِها لقدرة الغير بالنسبة لهذا الأثر
فبانَ لكَ بهذا : أنَّ صفة التأثيرِ والاختراع للكائناتِ مِنْ خواص مولانا جل وعزَّ التي لا يشاركه فيها شيءٌ مِنْ جميع ما سواه .
قوله : ( فلا أثر إذاً لقدرةِ المخلوقِ . . . ) إلى آخره : هذا نتيجة عمَّا قبلَهُ ؛ يعني : أنَّهُ لمَّا ثبت بالبرهان وجوب انفرادِهِ تعالى باختراع الكائناتِ ابتداءً بلا واسطةٍ .. لزمَ لذلكَ أنَّ القدرةَ التي خلقها الله تعالى في بعض الموجوداتِ كالحيواناتِ لا أثر لها ألبتة في حركة ولا سكون ولا غيرهما عموماً ، بل ذواتُ تلك الحيوانات ، وما فيها مِنَ القوَّةِ والقدرة ، وما صاحبَ ذلكَ مِنَ الحركة والسكون وغيرهما مِنَ الأفعالِ . . كلُّ ذلكَ واقع بخلْقِ اللهِ تعالى بلا واسطةٍ ولا أثر لبعض ذلك في بعض ، وإنما ذواتُ العالم كله مخلوقة الله تعالى ، وهي أوعيةٌ لآثارِ قدرتِهِ جلَّ وعزّ ، يُوجِدُ سبحانه وتعالى في كلِّ ذاتٍ منها مِنَ الأعراض ما شاءَ .
فمِنَ الذواتِ ما يُوجِدُ اللهُ تعالى فيهِ عَرَضَ الحركة والسكون أو نحوهما منفرداً عن عَرَضِ القدرةِ الحادثة المتعلقة بهِ ؛ كما في حركة الارتعاش ونحوها ، وتُسمَّى هذه الذات حينئذٍ في الاصطلاح : مجبورةً .
ومِنَ الذواتِ ما يُوجِدُ اللهُ تعالى فيهِ عَرَضَ الحركة والسكون أو نحوهما ، ويُوجِدُ معَ ذلكَ عَرَضاً يُسمَّى قدرةً تقارنُ ذلك الفعل ، وتتعلَّقُ بهِ مِنْ غيرِ تأثير لها فيهِ أصلاً ، وإنَّما الذاتُ تُحِسُّ بِهِ تَيَسُّراً للفعل وتمكناً منه ، ومِنْ أجل ذلكَ تُسمَّى الذات المخلوق فيها هذا العرَضُ في الاصطلاح : مختارة
ثم كلُّ واحدٍ مِنْ هذين القسمين قد يخلق الله تعالى له شعوراً بما خلق فيهِ مِنْ هذهِ الأعراض ، وقد يخلقُ له نوماً أو ذُهولاً عن ذلكَ ، يخلقُ سبحانَهُ ما يشاء ويختارُ ، ولا يُسأل عما يفعلُ .
And as for if their difference is supposed — such as we assume the attachment of the power of the Master, Glorious and Exalted, and His will to the movement of a body at a certain time, and the attachment of the power of another to the stillness of that body at that specific time — then we say: it is inevitable:
Either both occurrences happen, in which case the conjunction of two opposites, namely movement and stillness, follows;
Or neither of them happens, in which case the inability of the Most High Creator follows, and also the bareness of that body from movement and stillness follows;
Or one of them happens without the other; if what happens is the capability of the other, then the incapacitation of the God, Glorious and Exalted, follows; and if what happens is the capability of the Master, Glorious and Exalted, then preference without a preferrer follows, and also the possibility of the incapacity of the eternal power follows, due to the assumption of its equality with the power of the other with respect to this effect.
Thus it becomes clear to you by this: that the attribute of effecting and creating of beings is among the special characteristics of our Master, Glorious and Exalted, in which nothing from all besides Him shares with Him.
His statement: (So there is no effect for the power of the creature ...) to its end: this is a result of what preceded it; meaning: that when it was established by proof the necessity of His exclusivity, Exalted, in creating beings initially without any mediation, it follows from that that the power which Allah, Exalted, created in some existing things like animals has absolutely no effect in movement nor stillness nor other things generally; rather, the essences of those animals, and what is in them of strength and power, and what accompanies that of movement and stillness and other actions... all that happens by the creation of Allah, Exalted, without mediation, and there is no effect of some of that in some; rather, the essences of the whole world are created by Allah, Exalted, and they are vessels for the effects of His power, Glorious and Exalted; He, Exalted, creates in each essence of them of the accidents what He wills.
So among the essences are those in which Allah, Exalted, creates the accident of movement and stillness or similar to them alone without the accident of the originated power attached to it; as in the movement of tremor and similar to it, and this essence is then called in terminology: compelled.
And among the essences are those in which Allah, Exalted, creates the accident of movement and stillness or similar to them, and creates along with that an accident called power which accompanies that act, and is attached to it without having any effect in it at all; rather, the essence feels it as an ease for the act and an ability from it, and for that reason the essence in which this accident is created is called in terminology: chosen.
Then each one of these two categories, Allah, Exalted, may create for it consciousness of what He created in it of these accidents, and may create for it sleep or heedlessness of that; He, Exalted, creates what He wills and chooses, and He is not asked about what He does.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on Sanusi's proof that God alone creates and on the classification of created acts. The commentator begins by presenting a hypothetical scenario: if two powers (one divine, one created) are assumed to be attached to contradictory effects on the same body at the same time (movement vs. stillness), then several impossible outcomes follow. First, if both effects occur, that would necessitate the conjunction of two opposites (movement and stillness), which is impossible. Second, if neither occurs, that would imply that God is unable to produce His desired effect and that the body is devoid of both movement and stillness, which is also impossible. Third, if only one occurs, then if it is the created power's effect, that would imply God is incapacitated; if it is God's effect, then that would be a preference without a preferrer, and also the possibility of the eternal power being incapacitated because it was assumed equal to the created power with respect to that effect. The only valid conclusion is that the created power cannot be truly effective; rather, the attribute of effecting and creating belongs exclusively to God. The commentator then explains the result: since the proof establishes God's exclusive creation, the powers created in creatures have absolutely no effect on any action, whether movement, stillness, or otherwise. All actions, along with the essences and powers of creatures, are directly created by God. The essences are merely vessels for God's power. The commentator then classifies beings into two types: (1) compelled (majburah) beings, where God creates the action (e.g., movement) without creating an accompanying power, such as in involuntary tremors; (2) chosen (mukhtarah) beings, where God creates the action along with an accident called power, which accompanies the action without having any effect—it only provides the creature with a sense of ease and ability, leading to the designation 'chosen'. Finally, the commentator notes that for either category, God may grant consciousness of the created accidents or may cause sleep or heedlessness, emphasizing that God does as He wills and is not questioned.

Key Terms

إرادة
ترجيح بلا مرجح
اجتماع الضدين
اختراع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That creatures have independent causal power to produce their actions.
Correction: This proof shows that no created power can truly produce an effect; all acts are directly created by Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, if only one of the two opposite effects occurs and it is the one attached to the created power, what follows?
A) Both powers are effective.
B) God is incapacitated.
C) The body remains in its original state.
D) Preference without a preferrer occurs.

Key Takeaway
Only Allah has the attribute of creation and effecting; no creature shares in this.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something you worked hard for, do you genuinely feel that Allah alone created that success, or does a part of you believe your effort had independent causal power? How can you train your heart to attribute every outcome solely to Him?
?
If no one besides Allah has any real influence, why do you still fear people's opinions or actions? What concrete step can you take this week to transfer your reliance from people to Allah alone?
?
The proof shows that any claim of real causal power for creatures leads to logical absurdity. Is there an area of your life where you still act as if your own power or someone else's power truly creates effects? How will you realign that belief with this truth?

Divine Transcendence

Classification of Created Acts: Compelled and Chosen
Classification of essences into compelled and chosen, with no causal role for created power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two categories of created beings—compelled (majburah) and chosen (mukhtarah)—and how the created power (qudrah) is merely an accompanying accident with no causal effect.

Core Idea
Creatures are either compelled or chosen, but in both cases Allah alone creates their actions.

Having proven that only God creates, the commentator now draws the implications: the powers He creates in animals have no actual effect. He then classifies beings into two types—those in which He creates the action alone (compelled) and those in which He creates the action along with an accident called power (chosen). This classification explains how creatures experience choice while still being under God's exclusive creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the conclusion from the proof
Start with 'قوله: (فلا أثر إذاً لقدرة المخلوق...) إلى آخره' to see that the commentator states the result: created powers have no effect whatsoever.
This is the foundation for the classification.
2
Understand the two categories
Identify the two kinds of essences: one in which Allah creates the act alone (compelled, like a tremor) and one in which He creates both the act and a power accident (chosen).
The power accident gives the creature a sense of ability, but it does not cause the action.
3
Note the terminology
Learn the terms 'majburah' (compelled) and 'mukhtarah' (chosen) and how they relate to the presence or absence of the created power accident.
The classification is based on the attributes Allah creates in the essence.
4
Reflect on divine sovereignty
The final sentence emphasizes that Allah may grant consciousness or heedlessness to either category; He is not questioned about His actions.
This reinforces the absolute creative authority of Allah.

وأَمَّا إِنْ قُدِّرَ اختلافُهما - كأن نفرض تعلُّق قدرةِ المولى جل وعزَّ وإرادته بحركة جسم في زمان كذا ، وتعلق قدرة الغير بسكون ذلكَ الجسمِ في ذلك الزمانِ المعيَّنِ - فحينئذٍ نقولُ : لا يخلو :
إما أن يقع الأمران جميعاً ، فيلزم عليه اجتماع الضدين وهما الحركة والسكون
أو لا يقعَ واحد منهما ، فيلزم عجز الباري تعالى عن ذلكَ ، ويلزم أيضاً عُرُو ذلكَ الجِرْمِ عن الحركة والسكون
أو يقع أحدهما دونَ الآخرِ ، فإنْ كانَ ذلكَ الواقع هو مقدور الغيرِ لزم تعجيزُ الإله جلَّ وعزَّ ، وإنْ كانَ الواقع مقدور المولى جل وعزَّ لزم الترجيحُ بلا مُرجُحٍ ، ولزم أيضاً جواز عجزِ القدرة القديمة ؛ لفَرْضِ مساواتِها لقدرة الغير بالنسبة لهذا الأثر
فبانَ لكَ بهذا : أنَّ صفة التأثيرِ والاختراع للكائناتِ مِنْ خواص مولانا جل وعزَّ التي لا يشاركه فيها شيءٌ مِنْ جميع ما سواه .
قوله : ( فلا أثر إذاً لقدرةِ المخلوقِ . . . ) إلى آخره : هذا نتيجة عمَّا قبلَهُ ؛ يعني : أنَّهُ لمَّا ثبت بالبرهان وجوب انفرادِهِ تعالى باختراع الكائناتِ ابتداءً بلا واسطةٍ .. لزمَ لذلكَ أنَّ القدرةَ التي خلقها الله تعالى في بعض الموجوداتِ كالحيواناتِ لا أثر لها ألبتة في حركة ولا سكون ولا غيرهما عموماً ، بل ذواتُ تلك الحيوانات ، وما فيها مِنَ القوَّةِ والقدرة ، وما صاحبَ ذلكَ مِنَ الحركة والسكون وغيرهما مِنَ الأفعالِ . . كلُّ ذلكَ واقع بخلْقِ اللهِ تعالى بلا واسطةٍ ولا أثر لبعض ذلك في بعض ، وإنما ذواتُ العالم كله مخلوقة الله تعالى ، وهي أوعيةٌ لآثارِ قدرتِهِ جلَّ وعزّ ، يُوجِدُ سبحانه وتعالى في كلِّ ذاتٍ منها مِنَ الأعراض ما شاءَ .
فمِنَ الذواتِ ما يُوجِدُ اللهُ تعالى فيهِ عَرَضَ الحركة والسكون أو نحوهما منفرداً عن عَرَضِ القدرةِ الحادثة المتعلقة بهِ ؛ كما في حركة الارتعاش ونحوها ، وتُسمَّى هذه الذات حينئذٍ في الاصطلاح : مجبورةً .
ومِنَ الذواتِ ما يُوجِدُ اللهُ تعالى فيهِ عَرَضَ الحركة والسكون أو نحوهما ، ويُوجِدُ معَ ذلكَ عَرَضاً يُسمَّى قدرةً تقارنُ ذلك الفعل ، وتتعلَّقُ بهِ مِنْ غيرِ تأثير لها فيهِ أصلاً ، وإنَّما الذاتُ تُحِسُّ بِهِ تَيَسُّراً للفعل وتمكناً منه ، ومِنْ أجل ذلكَ تُسمَّى الذات المخلوق فيها هذا العرَضُ في الاصطلاح : مختارة

And as for if their difference is supposed — such as we assume the attachment of the power of the Master, Glorious and Exalted, and His will to the movement of a body at a certain time, and the attachment of the power of another to the stillness of that body at that specific time — then we say: it is inevitable:
Either both occurrences happen, in which case the conjunction of two opposites, namely movement and stillness, follows;
Or neither of them happens, in which case the inability of the Most High Creator follows, and also the bareness of that body from movement and stillness follows;
Or one of them happens without the other; if what happens is the capability of the other, then the incapacitation of the God, Glorious and Exalted, follows; and if what happens is the capability of the Master, Glorious and Exalted, then preference without a preferrer follows, and also the possibility of the incapacity of the eternal power follows, due to the assumption of its equality with the power of the other with respect to this effect.
Thus it becomes clear to you by this: that the attribute of effecting and creating of beings is among the special characteristics of our Master, Glorious and Exalted, in which nothing from all besides Him shares with Him.
His statement: (So there is no effect for the power of the creature ...) to its end: this is a result of what preceded it; meaning: that when it was established by proof the necessity of His exclusivity, Exalted, in creating beings initially without any mediation, it follows from that that the power which Allah, Exalted, created in some existing things like animals has absolutely no effect in movement nor stillness nor other things generally; rather, the essences of those animals, and what is in them of strength and power, and what accompanies that of movement and stillness and other actions... all that happens by the creation of Allah, Exalted, without mediation, and there is no effect of some of that in some; rather, the essences of the whole world are created by Allah, Exalted, and they are vessels for the effects of His power, Glorious and Exalted; He, Exalted, creates in each essence of them of the accidents what He wills.
So among the essences are those in which Allah, Exalted, creates the accident of movement and stillness or similar to them alone without the accident of the originated power attached to it; as in the movement of tremor and similar to it, and this essence is then called in terminology: compelled.
And among the essences are those in which Allah, Exalted, creates the accident of movement and stillness or similar to them, and creates along with that an accident called power which accompanies that act, and is attached to it without having any effect in it at all; rather, the essence feels it as an ease for the act and an ability from it, and for that reason the essence in which this accident is created is called in terminology: chosen.
Then each one of these two categories, Allah, Exalted, may create for it consciousness of what He created in it of these accidents, and may create for it sleep or heedlessness of that; He, Exalted, creates what He wills and chooses, and He is not asked about what He does.

This passage is a commentary on Sanusi's proof that God alone creates and on the classification of created acts. The commentator begins by presenting a hypothetical scenario: if two powers (one divine, one created) are assumed to be attached to contradictory effects on the same body at the same time (movement vs. stillness), then several impossible outcomes follow. Checkpoint
What distinguishes a 'chosen' essence (mukhtarah) from a 'compelled' one (majburah)?
A) In the chosen, the creature's power causes the action.
B) In the chosen, Allah creates the action alone without any power accident.
C) In the chosen, Allah creates both the action and a power accident that gives a sense of ability.
D) In the chosen, the creature has free will independent of Allah's creation.

Key Takeaway
Allah alone creates all actions; the two types of essences differ only in the presence or absence of a power accident that gives a feeling of choice, not in any causal power.

?

Divine Transcendence

Obedience and Disobedience Are Signs, Not Causes, of Reward and Punishment
Sanusi explains that reward and punishment are not caused by actions but are directly from Allah, with actions as signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi holds that human actions do not cause divine reward or punishment but are merely signs of Allah's prior decree.

Core Idea
Actions are signs of reward and punishment, not their causes.

Sanusi begins by stating a key principle of Ash'ari theology: reward and punishment are not causally determined by human actions. Instead, obedience and disobedience are signs created by Allah that indicate His choice. This lesson unpacks that principle and its foundation in divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its translation. Notice how Sanusi frames the relationship between actions and reward.
The heading in brackets is part of the source text.
2
Identify the main claim
Sanusi asserts that obedience and disobedience are 'amārāt' (signs), not 'ʿilal' (causes). Find this claim and note the supporting arguments.
The Quranic verse 21:23 is invoked to show Allah is not questioned.
3
Understand the proof from divine action
Sanusi argues that since all creatures' essences, attributes, and actions are directly created by Allah, they are equal before Him with no causal influence among them. Reward and punishment, being His actions, must follow the same rule.
This establishes that actions have no effect on reward/punishment.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Reward and punishment occur solely by Allah's choice, with no effect from any creature's action. Actions are merely signs that indicate what Allah has already chosen.
This guards against the misconception of earning reward through actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[الطاعة والمعصية أمارتان على الثواب والعقابِ لا علةٌ لهما ] والثواب والعقاب لا سبب لهما عقلاً ، وإنَّما الطاعةُ والمعصية أمارتان مخلوقتانِ اللهِ تعالى بلا واسطةٍ مُعِينَةٍ مِنَ العبد ، تدلانِ شرعاً على ما اختار سبحانه وتعالى مِنَ الثواب والعقاب ، ولو عَكَسَ سبحانه في دلالتهما ، أو أتابَ أو عاقبَ بدءاً بلا سَبْقِ أمارةٍ . . لحسُنَ ذلكَ منهُ جلَّ وعزَّ ، لَا يُسْلُ عَمَّا يَفْعَلُ ﴾ [الأنبياء : ٢٣] . يعني : أَنَّهُ لما تقرَّرَ أَنَّ ذواتِ المخلوقات كلها وجميع صفاتها وأفعالها أفعال لمولانا جل وعزَّ ، مخلوقةٌ له بلا واسطةٍ ولا غرض ولا أثر لكل ما سواه في أثر ما على العموم .. لزم استواء الأفعال كلها بالنسبة إليه جلَّ وعزَّ ، واستواؤُها أيضاً فيما بينها باعتبارِ أَنَّهُ لا أثر لبعضها في بعض ، لا باختيار ولا بطبع ولا بتعليل . ولا خفاءَ أنَّ الثواب والعقابَ فعلانِ مِنْ أفعالِ مولانا جلَّ وعزَّ ، فوجب أن يكونا واقعين بمحْضِ اختيارِهِ تعالى ، ولا أثر لكلِّ ما سواه مِنْ ذات أو فعل في شيءٍ منهما ، لا باختيار ولا بطبع ولا بتعليلٍ ، كما أنَّ ذلك حكم سائر أفعالِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ .
[Obedience and disobedience are signs of reward and punishment, not a cause for them] And reward and punishment have no cause rationally, but rather obedience and disobedience are two signs created by Allah Almighty without any assisting intermediary from the servant, indicating by divine law what He, Glorious and Exalted, has chosen of reward and punishment. And if He, Glorious, were to reverse their indication, or reward or punish initially without the precedence of a sign, that would be good from Him, Glorious and Exalted. 'He is not questioned about what He does' [Qur'an 21:23]. Meaning: when it is established that the essences of all creatures and all their attributes and actions are actions of our Master, Glorious and Exalted, created by Him without intermediary, purpose, or effect for anyone other than Him in any effect generally, then the equality of all actions with respect to Him, Glorious and Exalted, follows necessarily, and their equality among themselves as well, considering that there is no effect of some upon others, neither by choice, nor by nature, nor by causation. And it is no secret that reward and punishment are two of the actions of our Master, Glorious and Exalted, so it is necessary that they occur by the sheer choice of Him, Exalted, and that there is no effect for anything other than Him—whether essence or action—in anything of them, neither by choice, nor by nature, nor by causation, just as that is the ruling of all His other actions, Glorious and Exalted.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal explanation of the relationship between human actions and divine reward/punishment. It begins with a heading stating that obedience and disobedience are signs (amārāt) of reward and punishment, not causes. Sanusi then elaborates: reward and punishment have no rational cause ('aqlan); rather, obedience and disobedience are two signs created directly by Allah without any assisting intermediary from the servant. They indicate by divine law (sharʿan) what Allah has chosen. If Allah were to reverse their indication, or reward or punish without any preceding sign, that would be perfectly good from Him, as He is not questioned about what He does (Qur'an 21:23). Sanusi then explains the underlying principle: since all essences, attributes, and actions of creatures are directly created by Allah without intermediary, purpose, or effect from others, all actions are equal in relation to Him and among themselves—no action has any effect on another by choice, nature, or causation. Therefore, reward and punishment, being two of Allah's actions, must occur solely by His choice, with no effect from any other being, whether their essence or actions, by choice, nature, or causation, just like all other divine acts. This passage guards against the misconception that human actions causally determine divine reward or punishment.

Key Terms
الأمارة
العلة
الثواب
العقاب
السبب العقلي
استواء الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human actions cause Allah to reward or punish.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that actions are only signs (amārāt) that indicate His prior decree; they have no causal effect.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the relationship between human actions (obedience/disobedience) and reward/punishment?
A) Actions are the rational causes of reward and punishment.
B) Actions are signs that indicate what Allah has chosen.
C) Actions earn reward by their own intrinsic merit.
D) Actions determine Allah's decision to reward or punish.

Key Takeaway
Obedience and disobedience are signs that indicate Allah's prior choice, not causes that determine reward or punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you subconsciously treat your acts of worship as if they 'earn' you Allah's reward, forgetting that even your obedience is created by Him and He owes you nothing? What would change today if you truly internalised that your good deeds are only signs, not leverage with Allah?
?
If Allah could reverse the signs and punish you without warning, would you still trust His wisdom and goodness? What does your answer reveal about your understanding of divine justice and your own entitlement?
?
When you sin, do you fear punishment as a natural consequence of your action, or do you fear the One who creates both the sin and the punishment? How does this lesson shift the focus of your accountability?

Reward and Punishment Are Known Only Through Revelation
Sanusi denies rational implication of actions for recompense.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari tradition holds that reward and punishment are not known through reason but only through divine revelation.

Core Idea
No action inherently deserves reward or punishment; only Allah's decree makes it so.

How do we know which actions bring reward and which bring punishment? Is it something we can figure out with our minds, or must we rely on revelation? In this passage, Sanusi clarifies a fundamental Ash'ari principle: the connection between our deeds and their recompense is not rational but purely a matter of divine will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how Sanusi contrasts the rational ('aqlan) and revealed (shar'an) perspectives.
2
Identify the key claim
Find where Sanusi says that acquired actions have no rational implication for reward or punishment. Underline the phrase that expresses this.
3
Understand the reasoning
Why is there no rational link? Because reward and punishment have no cause or proof in reason; they are based solely on the Legislator's decree and choice.
4
Recognize the counterview refuted
This passage rejects the Mu'tazilite view that actions are intrinsically good or evil and thus rationally necessitate reward or punishment.
5
Apply the principle
Consider an action like prayer. According to this passage, prayer does not rationally deserve reward; it is only because Allah has decreed it so that we expect reward. This underscores divine sovereignty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وأمارة الثواب والعقاب شرعاً ) يعني : وأما عقلاً فلا دَلالة للأعمال الكسبيَّةِ على ثواب ولا عقاب؛ لما قدَّمْنا أَوَّلاً أَنَّ الثوابَ والعقاب لا علَّةَ لهما ولا دليل عقلاً، وإنَّما الأعمال الكسبيَّةُ دلَّتْ عليها بحسَبِ جَعْلِ الشارع واختيارِهِ ، بلا ربط في ذلك ولا علاقة عقليّة أصلاً .
His saying: 'And the sign of reward and punishment is by revelation (shar'an)' means: As for rationally, there is no implication of the acquired actions upon reward or punishment; because we have mentioned earlier that reward and punishment have no cause and no rational proof, but rather the acquired actions indicate them according to the Legislator's decree and choice, with no rational connection or relation at all.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage clarifies that the relationship between actions and their recompense is purely based on divine decree, not rational necessity. The phrase 'amara (sign) refers to the indication that leads to knowledge of reward and punishment. The author states that rationally ('aqlan), acquired actions (a'mal kasbiyya) do not imply reward or punishment. This is because reward and punishment are not necessitated by the nature of actions; they are free grants from God. The only basis for the connection is the Legislator's (shari') decree and choice. There is no rational cause (illa) or proof (dalil) that would make an action deserving of reward or punishment in itself. This guards against the Mu'tazilite view that actions intrinsically deserve recompense.

Key Terms
أمارة
ثواب
عقاب
شرعاً
عقلاً
جعل الشارع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Good actions naturally deserve reward, and bad actions naturally deserve punishment, independent of revelation.
Correction: Sanusi asserts that no rational connection exists; reward and punishment are only known through divine decree and choice.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the basis for acquired actions indicating reward or punishment?
A) The rational goodness of the actions.
B) The decree and choice of the Legislator.
C) The intrinsic worth of the actions.
D) The servant's intention.

Key Takeaway
Reward and punishment are not known through reason but solely through revelation, because actions have no rational connection to recompense—only Allah's decree establishes it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you secretly believe that your good deeds obligate Allah to reward you? How does this passage challenge that sense of entitlement?
?
When you sin, do you assume punishment is automatic or deserved? What does this passage say about that assumption, and how should it change your attitude toward repentance?
?
If reward and punishment depend solely on Allah's decree, how does that reshape the way you approach worship—do you obey out of love and hope rather than a demand for wages?

Compelled in a Mould of Choice: The Two Aspects
Sanusi defines the two aspects of the servant: compelled and chosen in appearance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari concept that the servant is both compelled (in having no real effect) and chosen (in appearance) due to God's custom.

Core Idea
The servant is a vessel, not a cause; choice is only apparent.

Sanusi begins by summarizing the Sunni position on human action. He presents a paradoxical description: the servant is compelled yet appears to choose. In this lesson, we unpack what 'compelled' and 'chosen' actually mean according to the people of truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage from 'وحاصل العبد القادر' to 'بحسَبِ الظاهرِ' and its literal translation. Let the author's own wording introduce you to the concept.
Notice the concise definition at the start.
2
Identify the two aspects
The passage clearly divides into the 'compelled' aspect and the 'chosen' aspect. Find where each is explained and note the key terms used.
Compelled: 'لا أثر له البتة' and 'ظرف'. Chosen: 'عادة مولانا' and 'عزم وتصميم'.
3
Understand the definitions
Dig into what 'compelled' means: no real effect, only a vessel. Then what 'chosen' means: God's custom of not always attaching action, creating aversion and determination. This is the core of the doctrine.
The term 'ظرف للحوادث' is crucial; the servant is a container, not a cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحاصل العبد القادر عند أهل الحقِّ : أنه مجبورٌ في قالب مختار : مجبورٌ مِنْ حيثُ إِنَّهُ لا أثر له البتة في أثر ما عموماً ، وإنما هو ظرف للحوادثِ والأعراض ، يخلق الله تعالى فيهِ ما شاءَ منها ومختار مِنْ حيثُ إِنَّ عادة مولانا جل وعزَّ لمَّا جَرَتْ مَعَهُ بعدمِ دوامِ موالاة الفعل عليهِ سيَّما حالَ خلقِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ فيه كراهية للفعل ، وإنَّما يمده تعالى بالفعل في بعضِ الأوقاتِ على حسب الحاجة ، وخصوصاً حال خلقِهِ تعالى لهُ عزماً وتصميماً على الفعل.. صار العبد بهذهِ العادةِ العجيبةِ الدالَّةِ على سعةِ قدرةِ مَنْ لا يشغلُهُ شأنٌ عن شأنٍ ، ووسعَ علمه كلَّ شيءٍ .. مختاراً مُتمكِّناً مِنَ الفعل والتركِ بحسَبِ الظاهرِ فسبحانَ القهَّارِ الذي لَطُفَ بعضُ قهرِهِ ، حتى عَزَبَ عن إدراكه كثير مِنَ العقول ، فضلاً عن الأوهام ، فاعتقدَتْ لجهلها بباطن الأمرِ معَ عظیم عجزها وشدَّةِ فقرِها.. أنَّها قد خرجَتْ في بعض تصرفاتها عن قبضة قهرِ الواحدِ الملك العلام، وهيهات هيهات ! أنَّى لها ذلكَ وهي حليف العجز العام ، والافتقار الحقيقي على سبيل الدوامِ ؟! ولهذا قالَ بعضُ الأئمَّةِ : أشبه شيءٍ بالعبد المختار في مخالفة الظاهر للباطن .. آلاتُ لُعبة الخيالي ؛ فإِنَّ الجاهل بأمرِها يظهرُ لهُ ببادي الرأْيِ أنَّها تتحرَّكُ وتسكن وتسعى ويحملُ بعضُها على بعض باختيارها ، حتى إذا عرف باطن أمرها وجدها مجبورةً على تلك [؟]
The summary of the capable servant according to the people of truth: he is compelled in a mould of choice: compelled from the perspective that he has no effect at all in any effect generally, and he is only a vessel for events and accidents, God creates in him whatever He wills of them; and chosen from the perspective that the custom of our Lord, Glorious and Exalted, has proceeded with him in not perpetually attaching action to him, especially at the time of His creating in him, Glorious and Exalted, aversion to the action, but He only supplies him with the action in some times according to need, and especially at the time of His creating in him determination and resolve to act... Thus the servant, by this wondrous custom indicating the vastness of the power of Him whom no matter occupies from another matter, and whose knowledge encompasses everything, becomes in appearance chosen, able to act or refrain. So glorified be the Overpowering One whose subduing is so subtle that many minds fall short of perceiving it, let alone imaginations, so they believed out of ignorance of the inner reality, despite their immense weakness and intense need, that they have in some of their actions escaped the grip of the subduing of the One, the Master, the All-Knowing. How far, how far! How could they, while they are the companion of absolute weakness and true need perpetually? For this reason, one of the imams said: The thing most like the chosen servant in the opposition of the apparent to the inner are the puppets of a puppet show; for the ignorant person, at first glance, thinks they move, stand still, strive, and carry each other by their own choice, until when he knows their inner reality, he finds them forced upon that [?]
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage explains the key Ash'ari concept: the servant is 'compelled in a mould of choice' (majbūr fī qālib mukhtār). Sanusi first defines the two aspects. The servant is compelled because he has no real effect (athar) on any effect; he is merely a vessel (ẓarf) for God's creation of events and accidents. The servant is chosen (mukhtār) in appearance because God's custom (ʿāda) is such that He does not continuously attach action to him; sometimes He creates in him aversion (karāhiya) to an act, and sometimes He supplies him with the action according to need, creating in him determination (ʿazm) and resolve (taṣmīm). Due to this custom, the servant appears able to act or refrain. Sanusi then praises God whose subduing (qahr) is subtle, causing many minds to fail to perceive it, leading some ignorant people to think they have escaped God's grip. He refutes this by exclaiming how far that is, as they are always characterized by weakness and need. Finally, he gives an analogy from one of the imams: the servant is like puppets in a puppet show (luʿbat al-khayālī). The ignorant observer thinks the puppets move by their own choice, but when he understands the inner reality, he finds they are forced.

Key Terms
مجبور في قالب مختار
أثر
ظرف للحوادث
عادة مولانا
كراهية
عزم وتصميم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ash'aris deny free will entirely, claiming humans are mechanical puppets with no sense of choice.
Correction: This passage shows that Ash'aris affirm a meaningful sense of choice in appearance, based on God's custom of creating aversion and determination. The servant truly experiences choice, even though he is not the real cause.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why is the servant described as 'compelled'?
A) Because he has no control over his actions at all
B) Because he has no real effect on any effect and is only a vessel
C) Because God forces him to sin
D) Because he lacks any sense of choice

Key Takeaway
The servant has no real causal effect; his sense of choice is a result of God's consistent custom of creating aversion or determination in him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make a choice, you feel as though you are the originator. After reading this passage, can you honestly say that feeling of origin remains? How does it change your awareness of God's immediate presence in every action you take or refrain from?
?
Sanusi says that God creates in you both aversion and determination. Think of a recent decision you struggled with. In that struggle, can you see God's custom working on you—creating dislike or resolve? Does this realization lead you to thank Him for guiding your heart, or does it unsettle you?
?
If you truly internalized that your 'choice' is only an appearance and that you have no real effect, how would your gratitude change? Would you still ask God for strength to do good, knowing He creates both the will and the act? Or would you fall into negligence? Commit today to recite 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' whenever you feel self-sufficient in a decision.

The Subtle Subduing and the Puppet Analogy
Sanusi praises God's subtle subduing, refutes human independence, and gives the puppet analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God's subtle subduing can be mistaken for human freedom, and why the puppet analogy illustrates the servant's condition.

Core Idea
God's subduing is so subtle that people mistake it for their own power.

After establishing the two aspects, Sanusi exclaims at the subtlety of God's subduing, which causes many minds to miss it. He then refutes those who claim to have escaped God's control and gives a vivid analogy from puppet shows. This lesson explores those final points.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage of praise and refutation
Read the Arabic from 'فسبحانَ القهَّارِ' to the end, and its translation. Notice the emotional tone: glorification, then a sharp refutation.
The phrase 'وهيهات هيهات' is a strong denial.
2
Understand why people mistakenly think they have free will
Sanusi explains that God's subduing (qahr) is so subtle that many minds cannot perceive it. Out of ignorance and weakness, people believe they have acted independently. Identify this reasoning in the text.
Look for 'عزَبَ عن إدراكه كثير مِنَ العقول' and 'اعتقدَتْ لجهلها'.
3
Analyze the puppet analogy
The imam's analogy compares the servant to puppets in a show. The ignorant observer thinks puppets move by themselves; the wise see they are controlled. Reflect on how this illustrates the servant's condition.
The analogy reinforces the 'compelled in a mould of choice' concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?
Imagine you woke up tomorrow completely convinced that every thought, decision, and movement is directly forced by God. How would that change the way you pray, work, or interact with others? What fears or habits would you need to surrender?
?
If the puppet analogy is true, then your most 'free' choices—like which sin to avoid or which good deed to perform—are also under God's control. Does this make you feel relieved or trapped? And what does your reaction reveal about your trust in God's wisdom?

Critique of Anthropomorphic Interpretations
Sanusi warns against literal anthropomorphic interpretations neglecting rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why literal interpretations of scriptural terms about Allah can lead to anthropomorphism and why rational proofs are essential for correct theology.

Core Idea
Literal scripture without rational proof leads to corporealism.

This lesson examines a critical mistake: taking Quranic terms like 'hand' and 'face' literally without understanding their linguistic context or applying rational proofs. Sanusi warns that such an approach leads to attributing physicality and direction to Allah. We will see why the proof of contingency (دليل الافتقار) is essential to avoid this error.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the strong warning tone in Sanusi's words.
2
Identify the problematic terms
List the anthropomorphic terms mentioned (hand, leg, face, eye). Consider why these terms, taken literally, can lead to a mistaken understanding of Allah.
These terms are often used metaphorically in the Quran.
3
Understand the proof of need
Grasp the 'proof of need' (دليل الافتقار): everything in the world is contingent and dependent on Allah. Reflect on how this proof should prevent literal interpretations.
If something has a hand or face, it resembles contingent beings.
4
Analyze the Quranic verses
Look at the two verses cited (20:127 and 6:91). Understand how Sanusi uses them to show the deficiency of mere verbal knowledge.
The second verse distinguishes between knowing Allah's existence and knowing His true attributes.
5
Summarize the lesson's takeaway
Write a one-sentence summary of why literal interpretation without rational proof is dangerous for tawhid.
Combine this with the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وربَّما تمسكوا بألفاظ لم يُحيطوا بمعانيها في اللغةِ ؛ مِنْ ذكرِيدٍ أو ساق أو وَجْهِ أو عينٍ ، وتركوا العلم بحدوث العالَمِ مِنْ جهة الاستدلال ، واكتفوا بمُجرَّدِ القول بأنَّ العالَمَ فعلُ اللهِ تعالى ، ولم يتأملوا دليل الافتقار في العالم بأسره ، فورطَهم ذلك الحملُ على الظاهر في الجسميَّةِ والمكان والجهةِ . ولو تأملوا دليل الافتقار في العالم لعلموا أنَّ المتّصف بهذهِ الصفاتِ كفردٍ مِنْ أفراد العالم ، يجب حدوثه وعجزه كسائر العالم . وَكَذَلِكَ نَجْزِى مَنْ أَسْرَفَ وَلَمْ يُؤْمِنُ بِشَايَاتِ رَبِّهِ [طه : ١٢٧] فهؤلاء عرفوا اللهَ مِنْ جهةِ القولِ ، لا مِنْ جهة الدليل ، وليس لهم حقيقة العلم بما يجبُ ويجوزُ ويستحيل عليهِ تعالى ، ﴿ وَمَا قَدَرُوا اللَّهَ حَقَّ قَدْرِهِ ﴾ [الأنعام : ٩١] أي : ما عرفوا الله حق معرفتِهِ ، فما نفى عنهم المعرفة بالكليَّةِ ، ولكنَّهُ قالَ : ما عرفوا اللهَ حقَّ معرفتِهِ ؛ أي : عرفوا وجوده ، ولم يعلموا الفَرْقَ بينَ وجودِهِ ووجود الحوادث بأدلة الحدوثِ في خَلْقِهِ
And perhaps they clung to words whose meanings they did not comprehend in the language, such as 'hand', 'leg', 'face', or 'eye', and they abandoned knowledge of the creation of the world through inference, and they contented themselves with merely saying that the world is the act of Allah Almighty, and they did not reflect on the proof of need in the entire world, so that literal interpretation led them into corporealism, place, and direction. And if they had reflected on the proof of need in the world, they would have known that the one described with these attributes, as an individual of the individuals of the world, must be created and incapable like the rest of the world. 'And thus do We recompense he who transgressed and did not believe in the signs of his Lord' [Taha 20:127]. So these people knew Allah verbally, not through proof, and they have no true knowledge of what is necessary, possible, and impossible for Him Almighty. 'And they did not appraise Allah with true appraisal' [al-An'am 6:91], meaning: they did not know Allah with true knowledge; He did not negate knowledge from them entirely, but He said: they did not know Allah with true knowledge, meaning: they knew His existence, but they did not know the difference between His existence and the existence of contingent things through the proofs of origination in His creation.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage is a critique of those who adopt anthropomorphic interpretations of scriptural terms (like hand, leg, face, eye) without understanding their linguistic meanings or context. These individuals stopped at the literal wording and neglected the rational proof for the world's creation (حدوث العالم). They relied solely on the statement that the world is Allah's act, without contemplating the 'proof of need' (دليل الافتقار) which demonstrates that everything other than Allah is contingent and dependent. This led them to affirm corporeality, spatial location, and direction for Allah. Sanusi argues that if they had examined the proof of need, they would realize that anything possessing such attributes must be like any other contingent being: created and incapable. He then cites Quranic verses (20:127 and 6:91) to show that such people know Allah only in name, not through true knowledge that distinguishes His necessary existence from the contingent existence of creatures.

Key Terms
دليل الافتقار
جسمية
حدوث العالم
ظاهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Literal interpretation of scripture is always correct regardless of context.
Correction: The passage shows that taking terms like 'hand' and 'face' literally without linguistic understanding and rational proofs leads to anthropomorphism, which contradicts divine transcendence.

Checkpoint
What mistake did the people described in this passage make?
A) They denied the existence of Allah.
B) They took scriptural terms literally without understanding their linguistic meaning and neglected rational proofs.
C) They rejected all scripture.
D) They believed in multiple gods.

Key Takeaway
True knowledge of Allah requires combining scripture with rational proofs to avoid attributing created attributes to the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite or hear verses about Allah's 'hand' or 'face', do you pause to actively seek a correct understanding grounded in proof, or do you passively accept whatever comes to mind? How can you change that today?
?
Sanusi says some people 'knew Allah verbally, not through proof'. Honestly examine your own knowledge: can you articulate a rational proof that distinguishes Allah's existence from created existence? If not, what step will you take to acquire that proof?
?
Think of a belief you hold about Allah (e.g., His mercy, His power). Is it merely inherited or based on a proof? This lesson warns that mere verbal acknowledgment without reflection leads to ignorance of His true nature. What will you do to ensure your knowledge is not empty words?

Two Forms of Shirk: Essence and Intercession
Sanusi distinguishes two kinds of shirk: multiplicity in God's essence and intercessory gods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two specific forms of shirk: attributing multiplicity to Allah's essence (as in Christian trinitarianism) and affirming intercessory gods (as in idol worship).

Core Idea
Shirk includes dividing God's essence and making intermediaries into gods.

Sanusi continues his discussion of tawhid by identifying two distinct categories of shirk. The first involves misrepresenting Allah's essence as multiple, exemplified by Christian doctrines of hypostases. The second involves setting up intercessory deities that are worshipped alongside Allah. This passage clarifies that shirk is broader than mere idol worship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the literal translation to understand the basic meaning before analysis.
2
Identify the two categories
Notice that Sanusi presents two kinds of shirk. The first involves multiplicity in Allah's essence; the second involves affirming other deities as intercessors.
The first is labelled explicitly as the shirk of the Christians.
3
Understand the Christian example
Reflect on how the Christian doctrine of three hypostases (aqānīm) that are supposedly one constitutes shirk by attributing multiplicity to Allah's essence.
4
Understand the second category
The second kind of shirk is affirming gods that are worshipped as intermediaries to Allah. This includes idol worship and veneration of angels.
5
Reflect on the broader definition
Shirk is not limited to idol worship alone; it also includes any conception that divides Allah's essence or sets up intercessors.
This passage guards against a narrow understanding of shirk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرك تتعدَّدُ فيهِ ذاتُ اللهِ تعالى : وذلك شرك النصارى في ثبوتِ أقانيمها ، وأنَّها ثلاثةٌ تخلُقُ بثلاثتِها ، وهي ثلاثةٌ واحدٌ ! نعوذُ باللهِ من الضلالة . والصَنف الآخرُ مِنَ الشركِ : إثباتُ آلهة تُقرَّبُ إِليهِ مَنْ عبدَها وعظَمَها ، وهذا هو عبادة الأوثان والملائكة
Shirk in which the essence of Allah is multiplied: that is the shirk of the Christians in affirming their hypostases (aqānīm), and that they are three, creating by their three, and they are three ones! We seek refuge with Allah from misguidance. And the other kind of shirk: affirming gods that are brought near to Him by those who worship and venerate them, and this is the worship of idols and angels.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage classifies two kinds of shirk (polytheism). The first kind is shirk in which multiplicity is attributed to the essence of Allah, which is the shirk of the Christians who affirm three hypostases (aqānīm) and claim that these three are one. The author exclaims against this as misguidance. The second kind is shirk by affirming other deities that intercede with Allah, which is the worship of idols and angels.

Key Terms
شرك
أقانيم
آلهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think shirk is only idol worship, not including theological errors about God's nature.
Correction: This passage shows that shirk includes attributing multiplicity to Allah's essence, as in Christian trinitarianism, which is not idol worship but a doctrinal deviation.

Checkpoint
What is the first type of shirk described in this passage?
A) Shirk of the polytheists who worship idols
B) Shirk of the Christians in affirming three hypostases in God's essence
C) Shirk of the philosophers in attributing actions to celestial bodies
D) Shirk of the Mu'tazila in human creation of actions

Key Takeaway
Shirk includes both dividing Allah's essence and worshipping intercessors, making it broader than simple idolatry.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever thought that merely believing in God's oneness is enough while you still rely on created beings as intermediaries in your heart? The second type of shirk is not just about idols—it includes any being you turn to as a 'god' of help. Where in your life might you be guilty of this without realizing it? Today, commit to examining your heart and replacing reliance on any created cause with direct trust in Allah alone.
?
When you hear the Christian doctrine of trinity, do you feel a self-righteous pride that you are not like them? But what about the subtle ways you multiply 'gods' by over-glorifying scholars, leaders, or even yourself? Choose one such attachment and actively break it today by reminding yourself that all power belongs to Allah alone.
?
The author seeks refuge from the first type of shirk. Have you ever earnestly sought refuge from shirk in your own heart? Today, make a sincere du'a asking Allah to protect you from both forms of shirk—especially the hidden ones that seem 'respectable' in society—and take one concrete step to purify your worship.

Refutation of the Claim that Allah Has a Modality
Sanusi refutes the Batiniyya claim that Allah has a modality unknown to others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why affirming any modality for Allah leads to a logical impossibility, either implying shape or genus.

Core Idea
Affirming a modality for Allah implicitly denies His oneness and uniqueness.

Sanusi confronts a subtle but dangerous claim: that Allah possesses a modality (kayfiyya) known only to Himself. While this sounds pious, it actually undermines tawhid. In this passage, he exposes the logical contradictions that follow from such a belief, showing that it either reduces Allah to a physical form or places Him within categories that apply only to created things.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Allow the author's argument to present itself.
Notice the logical structure: two conditional scenarios.
2
Identify the two possibilities
Sanusi examines two possibilities for the alleged modality: either it is in Allah's essence, or it is in His attributes. Identify each and note the consequence that follows.
The modality cannot be neither; it must be one or the other.
3
Understand why each is impossible
For the essence: modality implies shape (shakl), which violates tawhid. For the attributes: modality implies genus and species, which cannot apply to the pre-eternal. Grasp why both are impossible for Allah.
This demonstrates that the Batiniyya claim is self-refuting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكما ذكرنا يعلمُ اللهُ تعالى نفسَهُ ، ومَنْ قالَ مِنَ الباطنيَّةِ : إِنَّ لَهُ كيفيةً لا يعلمها إلا هو. فقد جَهِلَ أَمرَ رَبِّهِ ، ولم يتحقَّقِ اليقينَ مِنْ قلبه ، ولو وقعَ السؤال عن تلك الكيفيَّةِ : أهي في ذاتِهِ ؛ فيكون ذا شكل ، وهذا يبطل الوحدانية في حقّهِ ، وإِنْ كانَتْ في صفاتِهِ فَإِنَّ الصفاتِ إِنَّما كيفيتُها تجنيسها وتنويعها ، والقديم ليسَ جنساً لشيء ولا نَوْعاً مِنْ جنس ، تبارك الله ربُّ العالمينَ
And as we mentioned, Allah knows Himself. And whoever among the Batiniyya says: 'He has a modality not known except by Him' - he has been ignorant of his Lord's affair, and has not realized certainty in his heart. And if the question arose concerning that modality: Is it in His essence? Then He would have a shape, and this invalidates oneness in His right. And if it is in His attributes, then the modality of attributes is their generic classification and diversification, and the pre-eternal is not a genus for anything nor a species of a genus. Blessed is Allah, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage refutes the Batiniyya claim that Allah has a modality (kayfiyya) known only to Himself. Sanusi argues that this statement shows ignorance of Allah. If the modality is in His essence, it would imply shape (shakl), which contradicts tawhid. If it is in His attributes, then modality means classification into genus and species, but the pre-eternal (Allah) is not a genus or species, as He is unique. Thus, affirming any modality leads to logical contradiction.

Key Terms
كيفية (kayfiyya, modality)
الباطنية (al-Bāṭiniyya)
وحدانية (waḥdāniyya, oneness)
شكل (shakl, shape)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that admitting an unknown modality for Allah is acceptable because it acknowledges His incomprehensibility.
Correction: Sanusi shows that this claim actually leads to logical contradictions (shape or genus) that undermine tawhid. True transcendence means denying any modality, not just saying it is unknown.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi reject the claim that Allah has a modality (kayfiyya)?
A) Because the Qur'an denies it
B) Because it implies shape or genus, contradicting tawhid
C) Because only the Prophet knew it
D) Because it is an innovation

Key Takeaway
Affirming any modality for Allah is impossible because it leads to shape (contradicting tawhid) or genus/species classification (impossible for the unique Pre-eternal).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine Allah in your mind, do you ever subtly picture a shape or form, even as you verbally deny it? How can you purge your heart of such hidden assumptions and truly affirm His absolute oneness?
?
Have you ever used the phrase 'Allah knows best' as a way to avoid thinking deeply about His attributes, covering up a comfortable ignorance? What would it take for you to have the certainty that Sanusi demands?
?
This lesson shows that a seemingly respectful claim about Allah can actually be ignorance. Is there any belief about Allah that you hold without testing it against the principles of tawhid? What will you do today to examine it?

Four Categories of Misguidance and True Knowledge of God
Sanusi lists four deviant groups and describes proper knowledge of God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four categories of theological misguidance and the essential components of true knowledge of Allah as taught by Sanusi.

Core Idea
True knowledge of Allah requires avoiding four pitfalls: anthropomorphism, attribute-negation, polytheism, and crediting others for actions.

Sanusi begins by identifying the main deviations that lead people away from correct belief. He then describes the positive knowledge that safeguards one from these errors. This passage serves as a concise summary of the fundamental principles of Islamic theology, emphasizing what must be affirmed and negated about Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the four groups
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the four groups mentioned and the specific error attributed to each.
The groups are: اليهود والمجسمة, الفلاسفة, النصارى والجاهلية, القدريَّة.
2
Understand each group's error
For each group, understand what they did wrong: tashbih (likening), ta'til (negation of attributes), shirk (association), and attributing actions to other than Allah.
Sanusi connects each error to a specific theological deviation.
3
Learn the components of true knowledge
The passage lists several attributes and negations that constitute true knowledge of Allah. List them and reflect on their significance.
These include existence, pre-eternity, unique dominion, majesty, sole creation and command, negation of deficiencies, and no kayfiyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نبيّاً ولتكذيبهم قوله تعالى : هَلْ مِنْ خَلِقٍ غَيْرُ اللَّهِ ﴾ [فاطر : ٣]، فهذه أصنافُ الضلالةِ ، فمَنْ سَلِمَ منها فقد عرف ربَّهُ حقَّ معرفتِهِ . فإِنَّ مَنْ لم يُشَبِّهُ ذاتَهُ تعالى كما فعلَتِ اليهود والمجسمة ، ولم ينف صفاته كما فعلَتِ الفلاسفةُ ، ولم يشرك معَهُ إِلهاً آخرَ كما فعلَتِ النصارى والجاهليَّةُ ، ولم يُضِف فعلاً إلى سواه كما فعلَتِ القدريَّةُ ومَنْ تبعَهم مِنْ كثيرٍ مِنَ الجهلةِ . فقد نوَّرَ الله تعالى قلبه، وأذهبَ العمايةَ عن بصرِ بصيرتِهِ ؛ عَلِمَ وجودَهُ وقدمه ، وانفراده بالملكِ وثبوت الجلالِ والعظمة له ، واستبدادَهُ بالخَلْقِ والأمرِ ، ونفي النقائص عنه ، وأنَّهُ لا كيفية له سبحانه ، وهذه نهاية المعرفة به سبحانه . جعلنا اللهُ ممَّنْ يعرفُ ربَّهُ ، ولا سلبنا حقيقة الإيمانِ بهِ ، وبملائكته ، وكتبه ورسله ، واليوم الآخرِ ، وبالقَدَرِ خيرِهِ وشَرِّهِ ، بفضله ورحمته
A prophet, and their denial of His saying: 'Is there any creator other than Allah?' [Fatir 35:3]. So these are the categories of misguidance. Whoever is safe from them has known his Lord with true knowledge. For whoever does not liken His essence - exalted is He - as the Jews and the Mujassimah did, and does not negate His attributes as the philosophers did, and does not associate another god with Him as the Christians and the Jahiliyyah did, and does not attribute an action to other than Him as the Qadariyyah and many of the ignorant who followed them did - then Allah has illuminated his heart and removed blindness from the sight of his insight. He knows His existence and pre-eternity, His uniqueness in dominion, the establishment of majesty and greatness for Him, His sole possession of creation and command, the negation of deficiencies from Him, and that He has no quality (kayfiyyah). This is the ultimate knowledge of Him - glorified is He. May Allah make us among those who know their Lord, and not deprive us of true faith in Him, in His angels, His books, His messengers, the Last Day, and in predestination (qadr), its good and its evil, by His grace and mercy.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is a classification and refutation of four major deviant groups in theology. It begins by referencing a verse (Qur'an 35:3) that denies any creator besides Allah, then states that there are categories of misguidance. The author then lists four types: (1) Those who liken Allah to creation (tashbih) – the Jews and Mujassimah; (2) Those who negate Allah's attributes (ta'til) – the philosophers; (3) Those who associate partners with Allah (shirk) – the Christians and pre-Islamic pagans; (4) Those who attribute actions to other than Allah (the Qadariyyah). Whoever avoids all these has true knowledge of Allah. The description of true knowledge includes: existence, pre-eternity, uniqueness in dominion, majesty, sole possession of creation and command, negation of deficiencies, and that He has no quality (kayfiyyah). The passage ends with a prayer for steadfast faith in these core beliefs.

Key Terms
تشبيه
تجسيم
تعطيل
شرك
قدرية
كيفية
معرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage is merely a list of heretical sects.
Correction: Sanusi uses the listing to define what true tawhid requires—avoiding each deviation and affirming specific positive attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group negates God's attributes?
A) اليهود
B) المجسمة
C) الفلاسفة
D) النصارى

Key Takeaway
True knowledge of Allah requires affirming His existence, pre-eternity, uniqueness, majesty, sole creation and command, and negating deficiencies and any quality (kayfiyyah) from Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Sanusi prays that Allah does not 'deprive us of true faith in Him' and in the Last Day. Have you ever felt that your faith is merely inherited or intellectual, not the kind that illuminates the heart? What one step can you take this week to turn that knowledge into heartfelt certainty?

Refutation of the Batiniyyah on Divine Quality
Sanusi refutes the claim of an unknown divine quality with a logical dichotomy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why claiming an unknown quality for God leads to absurdities such as form or classification, and how divine unity precludes any quality.

Core Idea
God's unity logically excludes any unknown quality.

This passage tackles a subtle theological error: the claim that God has a quality (kayfiyyah) known only to Him. The author shows that such a claim, if taken seriously, forces impossible conclusions about God's essence or attributes. Using the example of the indivisible atom, the argument underscores that true simplicity cannot have qualities. The commentator then explains how all discussions of God's necessary attributes implicitly show what is impossible for Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to understand the flow of the argument.
Notice the two-part structure: the refutation itself and the commentator's explanatory note.
2
Identify the two options for the quality
The author presents two possibilities: the quality is in God's essence or in His attributes. Trace the reasoning for each case.
If in essence → form → contradicts tawhid. If in attributes → implies genus/species → impossible for the Eternal.
3
Understand the jawhar fard analogy
The indivisible atom (jawhar fard) has no length, width, or shape, so it has no quality. This illustrates that simplicity precludes quality.
This is a logical example, not a statement about physics.
4
Grasp the commentator's implication argument
The commentator notes that all previous discussions proving necessary attributes also implicitly prove impossibility of their opposites.
This ties the specific refutation to the broader structure of the creed.

وكما ذكرنا يعلمُ الله تعالى نفسَهُ ، ومَنْ قالَ مِنَ الباطنيَّةِ : إِنَّ لَهُ كيفيةً لا يعلمها إلا هو. فقد جَهِلَ أَمرَ رَبِّهِ ، ولم يتحقَّقِ اليقينَ مِنْ قلبه، ولو وقعَ السؤال عن تلك الكيفيَّةِ : أهي في ذاتِهِ ؛ فيكون ذا شكل ، وهذا يبطل الوحدانية في حقّهِ ، وإِنْ كانَتْ في صفاتِهِ فَإِنَّ الصفاتِ إِنَّما كيفيتُها تجنيسها وتنويعها ، والقديم ليسَ جنساً لشيء ولا نَوْعاً مِنْ جنس ، تبارك الله ربُّ العالمينَ . والمخلوقاتُ إنَّما تتكيَّفُ إذا ائتلفَتْ وتشكَّلَتْ ، ولهذا الجوهر الفردُ لا كيفَ لهُ ؛ إذْ لا طولَ لهُ ولا عَرضَ ولا شكل ، ومَنْ ثبَتَتْ وحدانيّتُهُ وجبَتِ استحالةُ كيفيَّتِهِ انتهى، وبعضُه بالمعنى، فعليك بتحصيل معنى هذا الكلام، وهذا الفصلِ مِنَ العقيدة، فإِنَّ فِيهِ فوائد وإنقاذاً مِنْ غمرات هلك فيها كثيرٌ مِنَ الخَلْقِ نسألُ الله سبحانَهُ السلامة والعافية إلى المماتِ في ديننا ودنيانا، وأن يختم لنا بما ختم بهِ للمقرَّبينَ مِنْ أهل معرفتِهِ بلا محنةٍ، إِنَّهُ وليُّ ذلك والقادر عليه، وهو ذو الفضل العظيم . قوله : ( فقد عرفت بهذه الجمل ما يجب في حقه تعالى وما يستحيلُ ) يعني بـ ( الجمل ) : مِنْ فَضْلِ إثباتِ وجودِهِ تعالى إلى هنا ، ولا شكّ أنَّ هذهِ الفصول وإنْ كانَ الكلام في أكثرها إنَّما توجَّهَ بالقصدِ الأولِ ودَلالةِ المطابقة إلى بيان ما يجب في حقه تعالى . . فهي تفيد بالمعنى ودَلالة الالتزام ما يستحيلُ في حقه تعالى ؛ إذ ما مِنْ صفةٍ يُعلَمُ وجوبها لهُ تعالى إلا وهي تستلزم أنَّ أضدادها وما يؤول إلى نفيها . . مستحيل عليه ، وذلك ظاهر ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق ، لا ربَّ غيره ، ولا خير إلا خيره ، وهو حسبنا ونعم الوكيل
And as we mentioned, Allah knows Himself. And whoever among the Batiniyyah says that He has a quality (kayfiyyah) known only to Him, has indeed become ignorant of his Lord's matter and has not realized certainty in his heart. And if the question is raised about that quality: is it in His essence? Then He would have a form, and this invalidates Oneness (wahdaniyyah) in His regard. And if it is in His attributes, then the quality of attributes is their generic classification and specification, and the Eternal is not a genus for anything nor a species from a genus – blessed be Allah, Lord of the worlds. And created things only become qualified when they combine and take form, and for this reason the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) has no quality, as it has no length, width, or shape. And for whom unity is established, the impossibility of His having a quality is necessary. End – and some of it is paraphrased. So you must grasp the meaning of this speech and this chapter of the creed, for in it are benefits and rescue from floods in which many of creation have perished. We ask Allah – glorified is He – for safety and well-being until death in our religion and our world, and that He seal for us with what He sealed for the close ones among the people of His knowledge without trial. Indeed, He is the guardian of that and able over it, and He is the possessor of great bounty. His saying: 'You have indeed recognized by these sentences what is obligatory for Him and what is impossible' – meaning by 'the sentences': from the beginning of establishing His existence up to here. And there is no doubt that these chapters, even though the discourse in most of them is primarily directed and by literal indication to explain what is obligatory for Him, they also imply by meaning and implicative indication what is impossible for Him; for there is no attribute known to be obligatory for Him except that it entails that its opposites and what leads to its negation are impossible for Him. And that is apparent. And with Allah is success – no Lord other than Him, and no good except His good. He is sufficient for us and the best disposer of affairs.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage presents a refutation of the Batiniyyah (an esoteric sect) who claim that God has an unknown quality. The argument proceeds as follows: If the quality is in God's essence, it would give Him a form (shakl), which contradicts tawhid. If it is in His attributes, then the quality of attributes would require them to be classified into genera and species, but the Eternal is not a genus or species. Then, the author uses the example of the indivisible atom (jawhar fard), which has no length, width, or shape, to illustrate that simplicity entails absence of quality. Whoever accepts God's unity must accept the impossibility of quality. The passage concludes with a commentator's note explaining that the preceding discussions (from the beginning) primarily demonstrate what is obligatory for God, but also implicitly show what is impossible for Him, as every necessary attribute excludes its opposite.

كيفية
وحدانية
جوهر فرد
استحالة
دلالة المطابقة
دلالة الالتزام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Batiniyyah claim that God has an unknown quality (kayfiyyah) known only to Him.
Correction: This leads to either form in His essence or classification in His attributes, both impossible for God. True unity precludes any quality.

Checkpoint
What does the passage argue about the Batiniyyah's claim that God has an unknown quality?
A) It is possible but unknown
B) It leads to form or classification, both impossible for God
C) It is true because God is unknowable
D) It is only about attributes

Key Takeaway
Because divine unity is absolute, any quality attributed to God is impossible, as it would entail form or classification.

?
The indivisible atom has no quality because it has no parts; God is even simpler. Do you treat your mental image of Allah as something vast and majestic but still somehow 'something'? What form or classification have you unwittingly assigned to Him in your heart?
?
Sanusi says this chapter is a rescue from floods that many perished in. Are you willing to examine every thought you have about Allah to ensure it does not imply a quality? What specific belief about Allah today needs to be corrected based on this passage?

The Indivisible Atom and Divine Transcendence
Commentator explains why indivisible atom lacks quality, then links to God's transcendence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the indivisible atom has no quality and how this principle helps establish God's absolute transcendence.

Core Idea
Quality requires composition; the indivisible atom—and God—have no composition, hence no quality.

This passage explores a profound link between physics and theology. The commentator argues that quality (kayfiyya) is a property that only arises when parts combine. Since the indivisible atom has no parts, it has no quality. The same logic applies to God, whose oneness is absolute: He cannot have qualities as creatures do. Understanding this saves one from deep errors that have led many astray.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source passage carefully, then its translation. Notice how the argument builds from creation to the Creator.
The passage begins with a general rule about created things.
2
Understand the indivisible atom
Grasp why the indivisible atom (jawhar fard) lacks length, width, and shape. This is because it is not composed of smaller parts.
This is a key concept in classical atomism.
3
Apply the analogy to God
The commentator draws a theological conclusion: if even the indivisible atom cannot have quality due to its simplicity, how much more does this apply to God, who is absolutely one.
4
Reflect on the warning
The commentator warns that misunderstanding this leads to serious errors. Consider why this doctrine is so important for protecting tawhid.
The passage ends with a prayer, showing the stakes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمخلوقاتُ إنَّما تتكيَّفُ إذا ائتلفَتْ وتشكَّلَتْ ، ولهذا الجوهر الفردُ لا كيفَ لهُ ؛ إذْ لا طولَ لهُ ولا عَرضَ ولا شكل ، ومَنْ ثبَتَتْ وحدانيّتُهُ وجبَتِ استحالةُ كيفيَّتِهِ ( انتهى (۱) ، وبعضُه بالمعنى ، فعليك بتحصيل معنى هذا الكلام ، وهذا الفصلِ مِنَ العقيدة ، فإِنَّ فِيهِ فوائد وإنقاذاً مِنْ غمرات هلك فيها كثيرٌ مِنَ الخَلْقِ نسألُ الله سبحانَهُ السلامة والعافية إلى المماتِ في ديننا ودنيانا ، وأن يختم لنا بما ختم بهِ للمقرَّبينَ مِنْ أهل معرفتِهِ بلا محنةٍ ، إِنَّهُ وليُّ ذلك والقادر عليه ، وهو ذو الفضل العظيم .
Created things only acquire quality when they come together and become formed, and for this reason the indivisible atom has no quality, since it has no length, no breadth, and no shape. Whoever affirms His Oneness, the impossibility of His having quality is necessary. (End.) Some of it is paraphrased. So it is upon you to grasp the meaning of this speech and this chapter of the creed, for in it are benefits and deliverance from floods in which many of creation have perished. We ask Allah—glory be to Him—for safety and well-being until death in our religion and our world, and that He seal for us with what He sealed for the close ones among His people of knowledge without trial. Indeed, He is the Guardian of that and the One capable of it, and He is the Possessor of great bounty.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a previous quotation (from Ibn Dahaq) about the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). The commentator explains that created things only acquire quality (kayfiyya) when their parts come together and take on form. The indivisible atom, being the smallest unit that cannot be divided, has no extension—no length, width, or shape—and therefore no quality. The commentator then draws a theological inference: anyone who affirms God's absolute oneness must also affirm that quality is impossible for Him, because quality implies composition and change, which are impossible for the Necessary Being. The passage concludes with a cautionary note that understanding this concept saves one from errors that have led many astray, and the commentator prays for divine protection and a good end. The key technical term is "al-jawhar al-fard" (the indivisible atom) and "kayf" (quality).

Correction: Quality arises from composition; God is absolutely one, so quality is impossible for Him.

Key Takeaway
The indivisible atom's lack of quality illustrates that quality depends on composition, which is impossible for God, affirming His absolute transcendence.

Seeing Allah Without Physicality
Negation of physical conditions for ru'ya and affirmation of spiritual perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine that seeing Allah in the afterlife is a non-physical perception requiring neither an organ, direction, facing, nor any physical condition.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah needs no eye, no direction, no facing—only a soul to perceive.

This short but dense passage from Imam Sanusi clarifies a key Sunni creed: the vision of Allah (ru’ya) in Paradise is spiritual, not physical. It rejects any anthropomorphic or materialist interpretation by negating bodily requirements. As you read, notice how the author systematically removes each possible physical condition, then affirms only a bare substrate.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage aloud
Read the Arabic sentence once to absorb its rhythm. Then read the English translation slowly, noting each negation.
The passage is one continuous sentence, so pay attention to 'لا' and 'ولا'.
2
List what ru'ya does NOT require
Identify all the physical conditions that are negated: organ (bunyah), direction (jihah), facing (muqābalah), emission of rays, extreme closeness/distance, thick veil.
These are the false assumptions some people might have about seeing Allah.
3
Understand what ru'ya DOES require
The passage states that ru'ya only requires an absolute locus (maḥall) in which it subsists. Think about what this means: a non-physical perceiver (the soul) that is capable of experiencing vision.
The 'maḥall' is a conceptual substrate, not a physical organ.
4
Connect to knowledge (al-ʿilm)
The passage ends by comparing ru'ya to knowledge: just as knowledge is not hindered by distance or veils, so too is ru'ya. Reflect on why this analogy reinforces the spiritual nature of this vision.
Knowledge is an immaterial attribute; vision for Allah is similarly immaterial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرؤية عند أهل الحق لا تستدعي بنية ولا جهة ولا مقابلة، وإنما تستدعي مطلق محل تقوم به فقط، وليست بانبعاث أشعة من العين، ولا يمنع منها قرب ولا بعد مفرطان، ولا حجاب كثيف، كما لا يمنع ذلك من العلم .
And vision, according to the people of truth, does not require an organ (bunyah), nor direction (jihah), nor facing (muqābalah). Rather, it only requires an absolute locus (maḥall) in which it subsists. And it is not by the emission of rays from the eye, nor does excessive closeness or distance prevent it, nor a thick veil, just as that does not prevent knowledge.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Sunni (ahl al-ḥaqq) understanding of the nature of seeing Allah (ru’ya) in the afterlife. It negates any physicalist or anthropomorphic interpretation: ru'ya does not require a bodily organ (bunyah) like an eye, nor a direction (jihah) such as up or down, nor facing (muqābalah) as in two things being opposite each other. Instead, it only requires a locus (maḥall) in which it subsists—a non-physical substrate, likely the human soul or self. It explicitly rejects the theory that vision occurs by emission of rays (in‘ibāth ash‘a‘ah) from the eye. Furthermore, physical conditions like closeness, distance, or a thick veil do not hinder it, just as such factors do not hinder knowledge (al-ʿilm). This underscores that ru'ya is a spiritual, non-corporeal perception.

Key Terms

جهة
مقابلة
محل
انبعاث أشعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that seeing Allah requires a physical eye and direction, or that it is an optical process.
Correction: The passage clarifies that ru'ya is spiritual: no organ, direction, facing, or rays are needed; only a non-physical locus.

Checkpoint
